RN Questions 
1.
A nurse is reviewing laboratory values for a client with suspected acute kidney injury. Which laboratory value is the earliest indicator of declining renal function?

A. Elevated creatinine  
B. Elevated BUN  
C. Decreased urine output  
D. Hyperkalemia  

Correct Answer: C  
Rationale: Decreased urine output often appears before significant changes in creatinine or BUN during early kidney injury.

---

2.
A client with left-sided heart failure reports worsening shortness of breath. Which assessment finding is most concerning?

A. Crackles in the lung bases  
B. Mild ankle edema  
C. Jugular vein distention  
D. Weight gain of 1 lb

Correct Answer: A  
Rationale: Crackles indicate pulmonary fluid accumulation and worsening pulmonary congestion.

---

3.
Which medication is classified as an ACE inhibitor?

A. Lisinopril  
B. Metoprolol  
C. Amlodipine  
D. Losartan  

Correct Answer: A  
Rationale: Lisinopril inhibits angiotensin converting enzyme, reducing vasoconstriction and aldosterone secretion.

---

4.
A nurse is assessing a client experiencing hypoglycemia. Which symptom should the nurse expect first?

A. Confusion  
B. Sweating  
C. Seizures  
D. Loss of consciousness

Correct Answer: B  
Rationale: Early adrenergic symptoms of hypoglycemia include sweating, tremors, and tachycardia.

---

5.
A nurse is caring for a postoperative client. Which finding requires immediate intervention?

A. Urine output 20 mL/hr  
B. Temperature 37.5°C  
C. Pain score 6/10  
D. Respiratory rate 18

Correct Answer: A  
Rationale: Urine output less than 30 mL/hr may indicate inadequate renal perfusion.

---

6.
Which electrolyte imbalance is most commonly associated with peaked T waves on ECG?

A. Hyperkalemia  
B. Hypokalemia  
C. Hypercalcemia  
D. Hyponatremia  

Correct Answer: A

---

7.
Which intervention is priority for a client experiencing anaphylaxis?

A. Administer epinephrine  
B. Give antihistamines  
C. Start IV fluids  
D. Administer corticosteroids  

Correct Answer: A  
Rationale: Epinephrine reverses airway swelling and hypotension.

---

8.
Which signs are associated with increased intracranial pressure? (Select all that apply)

A. Vomiting  
B. Bradycardia  
C. Hypertension  
D. Decreased LOC  
E. Fever  

Correct Answers: A B C D

---

9.
A nurse is teaching a client about warfarin therapy. Which statement indicates understanding?

A. “I will avoid foods high in vitamin K.”  
B. “I should take aspirin daily.”  
C. “I will increase my sodium intake.”  
D. “I should take the medication only when symptoms occur.”

Correct Answer: A

---

10.
A nurse is assessing a newborn immediately after delivery. Which finding is most concerning?

A. Heart rate 120  
B. Respiratory rate 40  
C. Central cyanosis  
D. Acrocyanosis  

Correct Answer: C

---

11.
Which condition is characterized by airway inflammation and reversible bronchoconstriction?

A. Asthma  
B. COPD  
C. Pneumonia  
D. Pulmonary fibrosis  

Correct Answer: A

---

12.
A nurse is caring for a client with diabetic ketoacidosis. Which intervention is priority?

A. Insulin administration  
B. Fluid resuscitation  
C. Potassium replacement  
D. Sodium bicarbonate

Correct Answer: B  
Rationale: Fluid replacement is the first priority to restore perfusion.

---

13.
A nurse is caring for a client with a chest tube. Which finding requires immediate intervention?

A. Continuous bubbling in the water seal chamber  
B. Drainage of 50 mL/hr  
C. Tidaling in the water seal chamber  
D. Occlusive dressing intact  

Correct Answer: A

---

14.
Which finding indicates hypocalcemia?

A. Positive Chvostek sign  
B. Muscle weakness  
C. Constipation  
D. Polyuria  

Correct Answer: A

---

15.

A. Respiratory depression  
B. Hypertension  
C. Hyperglycemia  
D. Tachycardia  

Correct Answer: A

D. Rosacea

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION:

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest question bank.

These questions must be stored under:

CONTENT_TIER: RN
EXAM_TARGET: NCLEX-RN (United States) and Canadian RN preparation
CATEGORY: Nursing – RN

IMPORTANT RULES:
• These questions belong ONLY to the RN tier.
• Do NOT place these in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
• RT questions are handled separately.
• These questions should appear for BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
• Store questions using the question type field so the exam engine can render them properly.

Supported question types:
multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie
priority

Difficulty levels:
moderate
hard

Now import the following questions.
QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate

A client presents with crushing substernal chest pain radiating to the left arm. Which biomarker is most specific for myocardial infarction?

A. CK-MB
B. Myoglobin
C. Troponin I
D. LDH

Correct Answer: C

Rationale:
Troponin I is the most specific biomarker for myocardial injury and remains elevated longer than other markers.

---

QUESTION 2
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

Which clinical findings are associated with pulmonary embolism?

A. Sudden dyspnea
B. Tachycardia
C. Chest pain
D. Hypotension
E. Bradycardia

Correct Answers:
A
B
C
D

Rationale:
Pulmonary embolism commonly causes sudden dyspnea, tachycardia, chest pain, and sometimes hypotension due to impaired circulation.

---

QUESTION 3
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

Which medication is classified as a loop diuretic?

A. Hydrochlorothiazide
B. Furosemide
C. Spironolactone
D. Amiloride

Correct Answer: B

Rationale:
Furosemide inhibits sodium and chloride reabsorption in the ascending loop of Henle.

---

QUESTION 4
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency Nursing
DIFFICULTY: hard

Four clients arrive simultaneously in the emergency department. Which client should the nurse assess first?

A. Client with asthma and wheezing
B. Client with suspected stroke and facial droop
C. Client with chest pain and diaphoresis
D. Client with abdominal pain and nausea

Correct Answer: C

Rationale:
Chest pain with diaphoresis suggests acute myocardial infarction and requires immediate intervention.

---

QUESTION 5
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Emergency Nursing
DIFFICULTY: moderate

Place the steps of basic life support in the correct order.

1. Begin chest compressions
2. Check pulse and breathing
3. Activate emergency response system
4. Apply AED

Correct Order:

2
3
1
4

---

QUESTION 6
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate

Which mechanism explains the action of metformin?

A. Increases insulin secretion
B. Decreases hepatic glucose production
C. Blocks intestinal glucose absorption
D. Increases glucagon secretion

Correct Answer: B

---

QUESTION 7
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

Which findings suggest increased intracranial pressure?

A. Decreased level of consciousness
B. Vomiting
C. Bradycardia
D. Hypertension
E. Dilated pupils

Correct Answers:

A
B
C
D
E

---

QUESTION 8
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard

SCENARIO:
A client presents with fever, hypotension, tachycardia, and elevated lactate.

Identify the condition, interventions, and monitoring parameter.

Condition Options:
Septic shock
Cardiogenic shock
Hypovolemic shock

Correct Condition:
Septic shock

Interventions:
Administer broad spectrum antibiotics
Begin fluid resuscitation

Monitoring Parameter:
Serum lactate

---

QUESTION 9
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate

Which hormone maintains pregnancy during the first trimester?

D. Oxytocin

Correct Answer: C

QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac

A client with hyperkalemia is placed on cardiac monitoring. Which ECG change should the nurse expect?

A. Flattened T waves
B. Peaked T waves
C. ST depression
D. Prolonged QT interval

Correct Answer: B

Rationale:
Hyperkalemia causes tall peaked T waves due to faster ventricular repolarization.

QUESTION 21

CATEGORY: Endocrine

Which clinical finding is most consistent with diabetic ketoacidosis?

A. Metabolic alkalosis
B. Kussmaul respirations
C. Bradycardia
D. Hypoglycemia

Rationale:
DKA produces metabolic acidosis leading to deep rapid respirations (Kussmaul breathing).

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be available to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.

These questions must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

QUESTION 41
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac

Which assessment finding most strongly indicates left-sided heart failure?

A. Peripheral edema  
B. Crackles in the lungs  
C. Jugular vein distention  
D. Hepatomegaly  

Correct Answer: B

Rationale:
Left-sided heart failure causes pulmonary congestion leading to crackles.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest database.

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be visible to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
They must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

REQUIRED FIELDS FOR EVERY QUESTION

question_number
type
category
stem
options
correct_answer_or_correct_answers_or_correct_order
rationale
difficulty
target_exams
content_tier

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

IMPORT THE FOLLOWING RN QUESTIONS WITH RATIONALES INCLUDED

QUESTION 201
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with acute left-sided heart failure is admitted with worsening respiratory distress. Which assessment finding is most consistent with pulmonary edema?

OPTIONS:
A. Jugular venous distention
B. Crackles throughout the lungs
C. Hepatomegaly
D. Ascites

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Left-sided heart failure causes blood to back up into the pulmonary circulation, increasing hydrostatic pressure and forcing fluid into the alveoli. Diffuse crackles are a classic sign of pulmonary edema. Jugular venous distention, hepatomegaly, and ascites are more strongly associated with right-sided heart failure.

QUESTION 202
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are commonly associated with diabetic ketoacidosis?

OPTIONS:
A. Kussmaul respirations
B. Fruity breath odor
C. Hyperglycemia
D. Dehydration
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
DKA causes metabolic acidosis, which leads to Kussmaul respirations. Ketone production can produce a fruity breath odor. Marked hyperglycemia causes osmotic diuresis and dehydration. Bradycardia is not a typical early finding; tachycardia is more common due to volume depletion.

QUESTION 203
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. A client with a new colostomy reporting mild incisional pain
B. A client with pneumonia and an oxygen saturation of 84% on room air
C. A client with a blood glucose of 68 mg/dL who is awake and speaking
D. A client two days postoperative with a temperature of 38.1°C

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Using ABC prioritization, impaired oxygenation is the most urgent. An oxygen saturation of 84% indicates significant hypoxemia and potential respiratory compromise. The client with mild hypoglycemia is symptomatic but currently stable and able to communicate. Mild postoperative fever and incisional pain are lower priority.

QUESTION 204
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication should the nurse anticipate administering first for a client experiencing anaphylaxis?

OPTIONS:
A. Diphenhydramine
B. Epinephrine
C. Hydrocortisone
D. Salbutamol

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Epinephrine is the first-line medication for anaphylaxis because it rapidly reverses airway edema, bronchoconstriction, and hypotension. Antihistamines and corticosteroids are supportive therapies but do not act quickly enough to treat life-threatening airway and circulatory collapse.

QUESTION 205
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Stroke
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Place the priority actions for a client with suspected acute ischemic stroke in the correct order.

OPTIONS:
1. Obtain a noncontrast CT scan
2. Assess airway, breathing, and circulation
3. Activate the stroke response team
4. Determine eligibility for thrombolytic therapy

CORRECT ORDER:
2
3
1
4

RATIONALE:
Initial care begins with stabilization of airway, breathing, and circulation. Once the client is stabilized, the stroke team should be activated to speed evaluation. A noncontrast CT scan is then obtained to differentiate ischemic from hemorrhagic stroke. Thrombolytic eligibility is determined only after imaging and assessment.

QUESTION 206
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which arterial blood gas finding is most consistent with respiratory acidosis?

OPTIONS:
A. pH 7.30, PaCO2 55 mmHg, HCO3 24 mEq/L
B. pH 7.48, PaCO2 30 mmHg, HCO3 23 mEq/L
C. pH 7.31, PaCO2 36 mmHg, HCO3 18 mEq/L
D. pH 7.50, PaCO2 48 mmHg, HCO3 35 mEq/L

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Respiratory acidosis is characterized by a low pH and elevated PaCO2 due to hypoventilation and carbon dioxide retention. Option A matches this pattern. Option B reflects respiratory alkalosis, and option C reflects metabolic acidosis.

QUESTION 207
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Infection Control
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which interventions are appropriate when caring for a client with active pulmonary tuberculosis?

OPTIONS:
A. Place the client in a negative pressure room
B. Wear an N95 respirator
C. Limit the client’s transport outside the room
D. Use airborne precautions
E. Wear sterile gloves for all contact

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Tuberculosis requires airborne precautions, including placement in a negative pressure room and use of an N95 respirator. Transport should be limited to reduce exposure risk. Sterile gloves are not routinely required unless a sterile procedure is being performed.

QUESTION 208
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which assessment finding most strongly suggests increased intracranial pressure?

OPTIONS:
A. Hypotension
B. Papilledema
C. Polyuria
D. Bradykinesia

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Papilledema reflects optic disc swelling due to increased intracranial pressure and is a classic neurologic finding. Hypotension is not typical; hypertension is more concerning in this context. Polyuria and bradykinesia are not hallmark indicators of ICP elevation.

QUESTION 209
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with fever, hypotension, tachycardia, altered mental status, and an elevated serum lactate level.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Septic shock
Cardiogenic shock
Neurogenic shock

CORRECT CONDITION:
Septic shock

INTERVENTION OPTIONS:
Administer broad-spectrum antibiotics
Initiate rapid IV fluid resuscitation
Restrict fluids
Prepare for immediate chest tube insertion

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS:
Administer broad-spectrum antibiotics
Initiate rapid IV fluid resuscitation

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS:
Serum lactate
Amylase
INR
TSH

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER:
Serum lactate

RATIONALE:
The client’s presentation is consistent with septic shock, which involves infection, tissue hypoperfusion, hypotension, and elevated lactate. Immediate priorities include early antibiotics and aggressive fluid resuscitation. Serum lactate is a key marker of perfusion and severity.

QUESTION 210
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

CASE:
A 64-year-old client arrives in the emergency department with crushing substernal chest pain radiating to the left arm, diaphoresis, and nausea. The client rates the pain as 9 out of 10.

QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which diagnostic result would most strongly support myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS:
A. Elevated troponin
B. Elevated sodium
C. Elevated albumin
D. Elevated calcium

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Troponin is highly specific for myocardial injury and is a key biomarker in diagnosing myocardial infarction. Sodium, albumin, and calcium levels do not confirm acute coronary damage.

QUESTION 2
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which medication should the nurse anticipate administering immediately unless contraindicated?

OPTIONS:
A. Aspirin
B. Furosemide
C. Regular insulin
D. Acetaminophen

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Aspirin is given early in suspected myocardial infarction because it reduces platelet aggregation and limits clot extension. This improves myocardial perfusion and is a time-sensitive intervention.

QUESTION 211
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which assessment finding is the earliest indicator of acute kidney injury?

OPTIONS:
A. Increased hemoglobin
B. Decreased urine output
C. Hyperactive bowel sounds
D. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
A decline in urine output is often one of the earliest clinical signs of acute kidney injury. Changes in serum creatinine may lag behind. The other options are not typical early indicators of worsening renal function.

QUESTION 212
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Electrolytes
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are consistent with hyperkalemia?

OPTIONS:
A. Muscle weakness
B. Peaked T waves
C. Cardiac dysrhythmias
D. Flaccid paralysis
E. Hyperactive deep tendon reflexes

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Hyperkalemia increases the risk of muscle weakness, paralysis, peaked T waves, and potentially life-threatening cardiac dysrhythmias. Hyperactive reflexes are not a classic finding; neuromuscular weakness is more typical.

QUESTION 213
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding in an infant most strongly suggests dehydration?

OPTIONS:
A. Sunken fontanelle
B. Increased tears
C. Peripheral edema
D. Weight gain

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A sunken fontanelle is a classic sign of dehydration in infants. Increased tears and weight gain suggest adequate or excess fluid status, while edema does not indicate simple dehydration.

QUESTION 214
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding is most concerning in a pregnant client with preeclampsia?

OPTIONS:
A. Mild dependent edema
B. Blood pressure 168/110 mmHg
C. Urinary frequency
D. Heartburn after meals

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Severe hypertension in pregnancy is a major warning sign for worsening preeclampsia and increased risk of maternal and fetal complications, including stroke, placental abruption, and seizures. The other findings are less urgent.

QUESTION 215
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which laboratory value requires the nurse’s most immediate action?

OPTIONS:
A. Potassium 6.7 mmol/L
B. Sodium 134 mmol/L
C. Hemoglobin 11.8 g/dL
D. Glucose 132 mg/dL

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A potassium level of 6.7 mmol/L is critically high and can cause fatal arrhythmias. This value requires immediate assessment and intervention. The other values are either only mildly abnormal or not immediately life-threatening.

QUESTION 216
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client reports severe epigastric pain radiating to the back. Which condition is most likely?

OPTIONS:
A. Appendicitis
B. Pancreatitis
C. Ulcerative colitis
D. Cholelithiasis without inflammation

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Pancreatitis classically presents with severe epigastric pain that may radiate to the back, often accompanied by nausea and vomiting. Appendicitis more commonly causes right lower quadrant pain.

QUESTION 217
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which clinical findings are commonly associated with pulmonary embolism?

OPTIONS:
A. Sudden dyspnea
B. Tachycardia
C. Pleuritic chest pain
D. Hemoptysis
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Pulmonary embolism often presents with sudden shortness of breath, tachycardia, pleuritic chest pain, and sometimes hemoptysis. Bradycardia is not a typical initial finding.

QUESTION 218
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Hematology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which laboratory value indicates thrombocytopenia?

OPTIONS:
A. Platelet count 48,000/mm3
B. Platelet count 175,000/mm3
C. Platelet count 240,000/mm3
D. Platelet count 320,000/mm3

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A platelet count below the normal range indicates thrombocytopenia. A count of 48,000/mm3 is significantly low and places the client at risk for bleeding.

QUESTION 219
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication is used to reverse benzodiazepine overdose?

OPTIONS:
A. Naloxone
B. Flumazenil
C. Atropine
D. Epinephrine

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Flumazenil is the antidote for benzodiazepine overdose. Naloxone reverses opioids, not benzodiazepines. Atropine and epinephrine do not treat benzodiazepine toxicity.

QUESTION 220
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

CASE:
A 71-year-old client is admitted with fever, tachycardia, hypotension, and confusion. Serum lactate is elevated. Blood cultures are pending.

QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which condition is most likely?

OPTIONS:
A. Septic shock
B. Stable dehydration
C. Nephrotic syndrome
D. Migraine

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
The combination of infection indicators, hypotension, altered mental status, and elevated lactate strongly suggests septic shock with systemic hypoperfusion.

QUESTION 2
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which provider prescription should the nurse implement first?

OPTIONS:
A. Start broad-spectrum IV antibiotics
B. Offer oral fluids
C. Administer stool softener
D. Schedule routine physiotherapy

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Early broad-spectrum antibiotics are a time-sensitive component of sepsis management and reduce mortality. Oral fluids are inadequate in a hypotensive client with suspected septic shock.

QUESTION 221
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication class is commonly used for rate control in atrial fibrillation?

OPTIONS:
A. Beta blockers
B. Proton pump inhibitors
C. Opioids
D. Antifungals

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Beta blockers slow AV nodal conduction and are frequently used for ventricular rate control in atrial fibrillation. The other medication classes do not address cardiac rate control.

QUESTION 222
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are commonly associated with acute ischemic stroke?

OPTIONS:
A. Facial droop
B. Unilateral arm weakness
C. Slurred speech
D. Sudden confusion
E. Bilateral fixed pupils

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Common stroke symptoms include facial droop, unilateral weakness, speech difficulty, and sudden confusion. Bilateral fixed pupils suggest a more severe or different neurologic emergency and are not a typical early stroke screen finding.

QUESTION 223
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which condition is characterized by chronic airflow limitation and alveolar destruction?

OPTIONS:
A. Asthma
B. Emphysema
C. Pleurisy
D. Croup

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Emphysema involves destruction of alveolar walls and loss of elastic recoil, leading to chronic airflow limitation. Asthma is usually reversible, while pleurisy and croup are different processes.

QUESTION 224
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which hormone lowers blood glucose by promoting cellular uptake of glucose?

OPTIONS:
A. Glucagon
B. Insulin
C. Cortisol
D. Growth hormone

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Insulin lowers blood glucose by facilitating cellular uptake and storage of glucose. Glucagon, cortisol, and growth hormone generally increase blood glucose.

QUESTION 225
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. A client with a respiratory rate of 7 breaths/min
B. A client with nausea after lunch
C. A client requesting pain medication for chronic back pain
D. A client with a temperature of 37.8°C

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A respiratory rate of 7 indicates hypoventilation and an immediate risk to airway and breathing. This takes priority over stable pain, mild nausea, or low-grade temperature elevation.

QUESTION 226
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: CPR
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Place the basic life support actions in the correct order after finding an adult client unresponsive.

OPTIONS:
1. Begin chest compressions
2. Check breathing and pulse
3. Activate emergency response
4. Apply AED when available

CORRECT ORDER:
2
3
1
4

RATIONALE:
After identifying an unresponsive client, the nurse checks for breathing and pulse, activates help, begins chest compressions, and applies an AED as soon as it is available.

QUESTION 227
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which hormone primarily stimulates milk production after birth?

OPTIONS:
A. Oxytocin
B. Prolactin
C. Progesterone
D. Estrogen

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Prolactin stimulates milk production, while oxytocin is responsible for milk ejection or let-down. Estrogen and progesterone play other reproductive roles.

QUESTION 228
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Shock
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are consistent with hypovolemic shock?

OPTIONS:
A. Tachycardia
B. Hypotension
C. Cool clammy skin
D. Decreased urine output
E. Bounding pulses

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Hypovolemic shock decreases circulating volume, causing tachycardia, hypotension, peripheral vasoconstriction, cool clammy skin, and reduced urine output. Bounding pulses are not expected.

QUESTION 229
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which condition is most associated with a barking cough and inspiratory stridor in a young child?

OPTIONS:
A. Bronchiolitis
B. Croup
C. Asthma
D. Epiglottitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Croup commonly causes a barking cough and inspiratory stridor due to upper airway inflammation. Bronchiolitis typically causes lower airway symptoms such as wheezing.

QUESTION 230
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which ECG change is most likely to occur first with hyperkalemia?

OPTIONS:
A. Flattened T waves
B. Peaked T waves
C. Prolonged PR interval
D. ST elevation

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
The earliest classic ECG change in hyperkalemia is tall, peaked T waves. As potassium rises further, conduction delays and widening of the QRS can occur.

QUESTION 231
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are expected in acute respiratory distress syndrome?

OPTIONS:
A. Severe hypoxemia
B. Bilateral infiltrates on chest imaging
C. Decreased lung compliance
D. Diffuse alveolar damage
E. Consistently normal oxygenation

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
ARDS causes diffuse inflammatory lung injury, resulting in severe hypoxemia, bilateral infiltrates, stiff lungs with decreased compliance, and diffuse alveolar damage. Normal oxygenation would not be expected.

QUESTION 232
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which symptom is most characteristic of appendicitis?

OPTIONS:
A. Right lower quadrant pain
B. Left upper quadrant pain
C. Painless jaundice
D. Severe flank pain radiating to the groin

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Appendicitis classically presents with right lower quadrant abdominal pain, often after initial periumbilical discomfort. The other symptoms suggest different conditions.

QUESTION 233
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Hematology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which vitamin deficiency is associated with pernicious anemia?

OPTIONS:
A. Vitamin K
B. Vitamin B12
C. Vitamin C
D. Vitamin D

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Pernicious anemia is caused by impaired absorption of vitamin B12 due to lack of intrinsic factor. This leads to megaloblastic anemia and neurologic complications if untreated.

QUESTION 234
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with sudden unilateral leg swelling, warmth, redness, and calf pain.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Deep vein thrombosis
Cellulitis
Heart failure

CORRECT CONDITION:
Deep vein thrombosis

INTERVENTION OPTIONS:
Administer anticoagulation as prescribed
Avoid massaging the affected limb
Encourage vigorous ambulation immediately
Apply direct heat for prolonged periods without assessment

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS:
Administer anticoagulation as prescribed
Avoid massaging the affected limb

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS:
Signs of pulmonary embolism
Visual acuity
Bowel sounds
Thyroid function

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER:
Signs of pulmonary embolism

RATIONALE:
The presentation is classic for deep vein thrombosis. Anticoagulation helps prevent clot extension, and massaging the limb should be avoided because it may dislodge the clot. Ongoing monitoring is essential for pulmonary embolism.

QUESTION 235
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Heart Failure
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

CASE:
A 73-year-old client with chronic heart failure presents with dyspnea, orthopnea, peripheral edema, and crackles at both lung bases.

QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which finding best indicates fluid overload?

OPTIONS:
A. Dry mucous membranes
B. Crackles at both lung bases
C. Hypoactive bowel sounds
D. Cool dry skin

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Crackles suggest fluid accumulation in the lungs and are a key sign of fluid overload in heart failure. The other options do not directly indicate excess intravascular or pulmonary fluid.

QUESTION 2
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which medication should the nurse most expect to administer?

OPTIONS:
A. Furosemide
B. Diphenhydramine
C. Regular insulin
D. Ferrous sulfate

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Furosemide is a loop diuretic commonly used to reduce fluid overload in heart failure. The other medications do not address the immediate pathophysiology of pulmonary and peripheral congestion.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest database.

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be visible to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
They must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

REQUIRED FIELDS FOR EVERY QUESTION

question_number
type
category
stem
options
correct_answer_or_correct_answers_or_correct_order
rationale
difficulty
target_exams
content_tier

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

IMPORT THE FOLLOWING RN QUESTIONS WITH RATIONALES INCLUDED

QUESTION 236
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication is used to reverse opioid overdose?

OPTIONS:
A. Flumazenil
B. Naloxone
C. Epinephrine
D. Atropine

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Naloxone is an opioid antagonist that rapidly reverses respiratory and central nervous system depression caused by opioids. Flumazenil reverses benzodiazepines, not opioids.

QUESTION 237
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are commonly associated with meningitis?

OPTIONS:
A. Nuchal rigidity
B. Photophobia
C. Fever
D. Headache
E. Pitting edema

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Meningitis commonly presents with meningeal irritation and systemic infection findings, including neck stiffness, photophobia, fever, and headache. Pitting edema is not a typical feature.

QUESTION 238
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. A client with suspected meningitis and a new petechial rash
B. A client with chronic arthritis pain rated 8 out of 10
C. A client with constipation for 3 days
D. A client requesting a blanket

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Suspected meningitis with a petechial rash may indicate meningococcemia, which can rapidly progress to sepsis and shock. This is an immediate high-risk situation requiring urgent assessment.

QUESTION 239
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which assessment finding is most characteristic of a tension pneumothorax?

OPTIONS:
A. Tracheal deviation
B. Bilateral crackles
C. Bradycardia with hypertension
D. Productive cough with sputum

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A tension pneumothorax creates increasing intrathoracic pressure that can shift mediastinal structures, causing tracheal deviation, respiratory distress, and hemodynamic instability. This is a medical emergency.

QUESTION 240
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Place the following sepsis interventions in the correct order for a newly identified septic client.

OPTIONS:
1. Obtain blood cultures
2. Assess airway, breathing, and circulation
3. Administer broad-spectrum antibiotics
4. Begin IV fluid resuscitation

CORRECT ORDER:
2
1
4
3

RATIONALE:
The nurse first stabilizes airway, breathing, and circulation. Blood cultures should be obtained before antibiotics if this does not cause a significant delay. Fluid resuscitation is urgent for hypoperfusion, and early broad-spectrum antibiotics are then administered promptly.

QUESTION 241
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which serum marker is most specific for myocardial injury?

OPTIONS:
A. Troponin
B. Sodium
C. Amylase
D. Bilirubin

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Troponin is the most specific and clinically important biomarker for myocardial injury and is central to the diagnosis of myocardial infarction.

QUESTION 242
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are expected in hyperthyroidism?

OPTIONS:
A. Weight loss
B. Heat intolerance
C. Tachycardia
D. Anxiety
E. Constipation

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Hyperthyroidism increases metabolic activity, producing weight loss, heat intolerance, tachycardia, and anxiety. Constipation is more associated with hypothyroidism.

QUESTION 243
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which assessment finding is most concerning in a child with respiratory distress?

OPTIONS:
A. Nasal flaring
B. Intermittent dry cough
C. Mild fatigue after play
D. Temperature 37.2°C

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Nasal flaring indicates increased work of breathing in children and can signal significant respiratory distress. It requires prompt assessment and intervention.

QUESTION 244
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding is most consistent with placental abruption?

OPTIONS:
A. Painless bright red bleeding
B. Painful vaginal bleeding with uterine tenderness
C. No bleeding and no pain
D. Clear amniotic fluid leakage only

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Placental abruption typically presents with painful vaginal bleeding, uterine tenderness, and increased uterine tone. Painless bright red bleeding is more typical of placenta previa.

QUESTION 245
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with severe shortness of breath, unilateral absent breath sounds, hypotension, and tracheal deviation after chest trauma.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Tension pneumothorax
Pulmonary edema
Asthma exacerbation

CORRECT CONDITION:
Tension pneumothorax

INTERVENTION OPTIONS:
Provide high-flow oxygen
Prepare for immediate needle decompression
Encourage coughing exercises
Place the client flat without support

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS:
Provide high-flow oxygen
Prepare for immediate needle decompression

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS:
Respiratory status
Bowel elimination
Serum glucose
Thyroid function

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER:
Respiratory status

RATIONALE:
This presentation is classic for tension pneumothorax. Immediate oxygenation and decompression are lifesaving priorities. Respiratory status must be monitored closely because deterioration can occur rapidly.

QUESTION 246
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

CASE:
A 23-year-old client with type 1 diabetes presents with abdominal pain, vomiting, dehydration, blood glucose of 28 mmol/L, and deep rapid respirations.

QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which acid-base imbalance is most likely present?

OPTIONS:
A. Metabolic alkalosis
B. Respiratory alkalosis
C. Metabolic acidosis
D. Respiratory acidosis

CORRECT ANSWER:
C

RATIONALE:
The client’s presentation is consistent with diabetic ketoacidosis, which causes metabolic acidosis from ketone accumulation. Deep rapid respirations are compensatory Kussmaul respirations.

QUESTION 2
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which intervention is the priority at the start of treatment?

OPTIONS:
A. Fluid resuscitation
B. Oral hypoglycemic medication
C. Restrict fluids
D. Administer sodium bicarbonate first

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Initial DKA management prioritizes IV fluid resuscitation to restore circulation and reduce severe dehydration. Insulin therapy follows, but volume restoration is the first immediate priority.

QUESTION 247
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding is most suggestive of pyelonephritis?

OPTIONS:
A. Costovertebral angle tenderness
B. Painless hematuria only
C. Isolated ankle edema
D. Bilateral wheezing

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Pyelonephritis is a kidney infection and often presents with flank pain or costovertebral angle tenderness, fever, and urinary symptoms. The other findings are not characteristic.

QUESTION 248
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are associated with heart failure exacerbation?

OPTIONS:
A. Orthopnea
B. Crackles
C. Peripheral edema
D. Weight gain
E. Polyuria

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Heart failure exacerbation commonly causes orthopnea, pulmonary crackles, peripheral edema, and rapid weight gain from fluid retention. Polyuria is not a hallmark feature of decompensation.

QUESTION 249
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication is a loop diuretic?

OPTIONS:
A. Furosemide
B. Spironolactone
C. Metoprolol
D. Losartan

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Furosemide is a loop diuretic that promotes sodium and water excretion. Spironolactone is potassium-sparing, while metoprolol and losartan are not diuretics.

QUESTION 250
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which assessment finding requires the nurse’s most immediate action?

OPTIONS:
A. New onset stridor
B. Pain score of 6 out of 10
C. Oral temperature of 37.9°C
D. Blood pressure of 138/84 mmHg

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Stridor indicates upper airway obstruction and threatens ventilation immediately. Airway issues always take priority over pain, mild fever, or stable blood pressure.

QUESTION 251
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which clinical finding is most strongly associated with bowel obstruction?

OPTIONS:
A. High-pitched bowel sounds and abdominal distention
B. Bradycardia and clear lungs
C. Hemoptysis and pleuritic pain
D. Jaundice and clay-colored stools

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Bowel obstruction often causes abdominal distention, pain, vomiting, and high-pitched bowel sounds early in the course. The other options point toward different body systems.

QUESTION 252
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Infection Control
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which precautions are appropriate for measles?

OPTIONS:
A. Airborne precautions
B. Negative pressure room
C. N95 respirator
D. Limit unnecessary transport
E. Standard precautions only

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Measles is highly contagious and requires airborne precautions, including placement in a negative pressure room, respiratory protection, and minimizing transport to reduce exposure.

QUESTION 253
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which disorder is characterized by demyelination in the central nervous system?

OPTIONS:
A. Multiple sclerosis
B. Myasthenia gravis
C. Bell palsy
D. Meniere disease

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Multiple sclerosis is a demyelinating disorder of the central nervous system. The other conditions involve different pathophysiologic mechanisms.

QUESTION 254
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Hematology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which laboratory value indicates a therapeutic INR for many clients taking warfarin?

OPTIONS:
A. 0.9
B. 1.1
C. 2.0 to 3.0
D. 5.5 to 6.0

CORRECT ANSWER:
C

RATIONALE:
For many indications, a therapeutic INR on warfarin is approximately 2.0 to 3.0. Values below this may be subtherapeutic, while much higher values increase bleeding risk.

QUESTION 255
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Place the following actions in order for an adult client experiencing anaphylaxis.

OPTIONS:
1. Administer epinephrine
2. Assess airway and breathing
3. Call for additional help and emergency support
4. Prepare supplemental oxygen and IV access

CORRECT ORDER:
2
3
1
4

RATIONALE:
The nurse first assesses airway and breathing because anaphylaxis threatens ventilation. Emergency support is activated, epinephrine is administered without delay, and oxygen and IV access are prepared to support ongoing management.

QUESTION 256
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which clinical finding is most consistent with pulmonary edema?

OPTIONS:
A. Pink frothy sputum
B. Right lower quadrant pain
C. Jaundice
D. Bradykinesia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Pulmonary edema can cause severe dyspnea, crackles, and pink frothy sputum due to fluid in the alveoli. The other findings are unrelated.

QUESTION 257
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which signs may indicate dehydration in a young child?

OPTIONS:
A. Dry mucous membranes
B. Decreased urine output
C. Sunken eyes
D. Lethargy
E. Weight gain

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Dehydration in children commonly causes dry mucous membranes, reduced urine output, sunken eyes, lethargy, and poor skin turgor. Weight gain would not be expected.

QUESTION 258
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which maternal finding is most concerning in the immediate postpartum period?

OPTIONS:
A. Saturating a perineal pad in 15 minutes
B. Mild uterine cramping with breastfeeding
C. Small amount of lochia rubra
D. Fatigue after delivery

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Saturating a pad in 15 minutes suggests postpartum hemorrhage and requires immediate intervention. Mild cramping and a small amount of lochia are expected postpartum findings.

QUESTION 259
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with unilateral facial droop, slurred speech, and right arm weakness that began 30 minutes ago.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Acute ischemic stroke
Migraine aura
Bell palsy

CORRECT CONDITION:
Acute ischemic stroke

INTERVENTION OPTIONS:
Activate stroke protocol
Prepare for urgent brain imaging
Offer routine bedtime medication
Delay assessment until symptoms resolve

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS:
Activate stroke protocol
Prepare for urgent brain imaging

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS:
Neurologic status
Bowel sounds
Peripheral edema
Serum amylase

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER:
Neurologic status

RATIONALE:
The client has classic signs of acute stroke. Rapid protocol activation and urgent brain imaging are essential to determine treatment eligibility. Ongoing neurologic monitoring is critical for detecting progression.

QUESTION 260
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

CASE:
A 68-year-old client with COPD presents with worsening dyspnea, productive cough, wheezing, and oxygen saturation of 86% on room air.

QUESTION 1
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which intervention is the priority?

OPTIONS:
A. Apply supplemental oxygen as prescribed
B. Restrict oral fluids
C. Place the client flat in bed
D. Delay treatment until chest x-ray results return

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
The client is hypoxemic and requires immediate support for oxygenation. Delaying treatment is unsafe. Positioning flat may worsen breathing.

QUESTION 2
TYPE: multiple_choice

STEM:
Which additional assessment finding would support COPD exacerbation?

OPTIONS:
A. Increased sputum production
B. Painless jaundice
C. Neck stiffness
D. Polyuria

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
COPD exacerbation commonly involves increased dyspnea, wheezing, and increased sputum volume or purulence. The other findings suggest unrelated conditions.

QUESTION 261
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding is most consistent with hypoglycemia?

OPTIONS:
A. Sweating and tremors
B. Dry warm skin and polyuria
C. Kussmaul respirations
D. Fruity breath odor

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Hypoglycemia typically causes adrenergic symptoms such as sweating, tremors, and tachycardia, along with neuroglycopenic symptoms like confusion if it worsens. The other findings are more consistent with hyperglycemia or DKA.

QUESTION 262
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are expected in myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS:
A. Chest pressure
B. Diaphoresis
C. Nausea
D. Shortness of breath
E. Increased appetite

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Myocardial infarction commonly presents with chest pressure, diaphoresis, nausea, and dyspnea. Increased appetite is unrelated.

QUESTION 263
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which electrolyte abnormality is most common in advanced renal failure?

OPTIONS:
A. Hyperkalemia
B. Hypokalemia
C. Hyperphosphatemia absent
D. Hypoglycemia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Advanced renal failure commonly causes hyperkalemia because the kidneys cannot excrete potassium effectively. This is clinically significant because it can cause life-threatening dysrhythmias.

QUESTION 264
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding in a client with a head injury requires immediate intervention?

OPTIONS:
A. One pupil suddenly becomes fixed and dilated
B. Mild headache rated 3 out of 10
C. Bruising on the forearm
D. Temperature of 37.4°C

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A suddenly fixed and dilated pupil can indicate rising intracranial pressure or brain herniation and requires urgent intervention. The other findings are far less acute.

QUESTION 265
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication class is losartan?

OPTIONS:
A. Angiotensin receptor blocker
B. Beta blocker
C. Calcium channel blocker
D. Loop diuretic

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Losartan is an angiotensin II receptor blocker used in conditions such as hypertension and some forms of heart failure. It is not a beta blocker, calcium channel blocker, or loop diuretic.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest database.

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be visible to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
They must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

IMPORT THE FOLLOWING RN QUESTIONS WITH RATIONALES INCLUDED


QUESTION 266
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication is most commonly administered first for suspected myocardial infarction unless contraindicated?

OPTIONS:
A. Aspirin
B. Acetaminophen
C. Metformin
D. Amoxicillin

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Aspirin is given immediately during suspected myocardial infarction because it inhibits platelet aggregation and reduces clot propagation, improving coronary blood flow.


QUESTION 267
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which findings are consistent with asthma exacerbation?

OPTIONS:
A. Wheezing
B. Shortness of breath
C. Chest tightness
D. Prolonged expiration
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Asthma exacerbations commonly produce wheezing, chest tightness, dyspnea, and prolonged expiration due to bronchoconstriction. Bradycardia is not typical; tachycardia may occur.


QUESTION 268
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. Client with sudden onset stridor
B. Client with mild nausea
C. Client with chronic back pain
D. Client requesting assistance with ambulation

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Stridor indicates upper airway obstruction, which threatens ventilation and oxygenation. Airway compromise always takes priority.


QUESTION 269
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding most strongly suggests Bell palsy?

OPTIONS:
A. Unilateral facial paralysis
B. Bilateral leg weakness
C. Severe headache with aura
D. Tremor in both hands

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Bell palsy causes acute unilateral facial nerve paralysis affecting facial expression. Other symptoms listed correspond to different neurological disorders.


QUESTION 270
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: CPR
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Place the following steps of adult CPR in the correct order.

OPTIONS:
1. Begin chest compressions  
2. Activate emergency response system  
3. Check responsiveness and breathing  
4. Apply AED

CORRECT ORDER:
3
2
1
4

RATIONALE:
After identifying an unresponsive patient, the nurse checks breathing and pulse, activates help, begins compressions, and applies an AED as soon as available.


QUESTION 271
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which clinical finding is most consistent with pancreatitis?

OPTIONS:
A. Severe epigastric pain radiating to the back
B. Painless jaundice
C. Right lower quadrant pain
D. Pleuritic chest pain

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Pancreatitis commonly presents with severe epigastric pain radiating to the back along with nausea and vomiting.


QUESTION 272
TYPE: select_all_that_apply

B. Positive Chvostek sign

D. Positive Trousseau sign
E. Decreased reflexes

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Hypocalcemia increases neuromuscular excitability causing tetany, muscle spasms, and positive Chvostek and Trousseau signs.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest database.

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be visible to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
They must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

IMPORT THE FOLLOWING RN QUESTIONS WITH RATIONALES INCLUDED


QUESTION 311
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which electrolyte imbalance is most commonly associated with life-threatening cardiac dysrhythmias?

OPTIONS:
A. Hyperkalemia
B. Hypernatremia
C. Hypercalcemia
D. Hypophosphatemia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Hyperkalemia disrupts cardiac electrical conduction and can cause peaked T waves, widening QRS complexes, ventricular dysrhythmias, and cardiac arrest. Potassium levels must be monitored closely because even small changes can significantly affect cardiac rhythm.


QUESTION 312
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which clinical findings are associated with acute respiratory distress syndrome (ARDS)?

OPTIONS:
A. Severe hypoxemia
B. Bilateral pulmonary infiltrates
C. Decreased lung compliance
D. Diffuse alveolar damage
E. Normal oxygen saturation

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
ARDS is characterized by diffuse inflammatory injury to the lungs, causing alveolar damage, poor oxygen exchange, stiff lungs, and bilateral infiltrates on imaging. Severe hypoxemia is a hallmark finding.


QUESTION 313
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. Client with new onset chest pain and diaphoresis
B. Client with constipation for 3 days
C. Client requesting sleep medication
D. Client with mild headache

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Chest pain with diaphoresis suggests possible myocardial infarction. This situation threatens circulation and oxygen delivery to vital organs and therefore takes priority.


QUESTION 314
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition is most commonly associated with demyelination of neurons in the central nervous system?

OPTIONS:
A. Multiple sclerosis
B. Parkinson disease
C. Alzheimer disease
D. Huntington disease

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Multiple sclerosis involves autoimmune destruction of myelin in the central nervous system, leading to impaired nerve conduction and neurological symptoms such as weakness, vision changes, and coordination problems.


QUESTION 315
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Stroke
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Place the following actions in the correct order when caring for a client with suspected stroke.

OPTIONS:
1. Perform rapid neurological assessment
2. Activate stroke response team
3. Obtain CT scan
4. Determine eligibility for thrombolytics

CORRECT ORDER:
1
2
3
4

RATIONALE:
Rapid neurological assessment confirms suspicion of stroke. Activating the stroke team ensures immediate coordinated care. CT imaging differentiates ischemic from hemorrhagic stroke before determining thrombolytic eligibility.


QUESTION 316
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which hormone is primarily responsible for lowering blood glucose levels?

OPTIONS:
A. Insulin
B. Glucagon
C. Cortisol
D. Growth hormone

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Insulin facilitates cellular uptake of glucose and lowers blood glucose levels. Glucagon and cortisol increase glucose levels through gluconeogenesis and glycogen breakdown.


QUESTION 317
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which findings may indicate septic shock?

OPTIONS:
A. Hypotension
B. Tachycardia
C. Altered mental status
D. Elevated lactate
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Septic shock results from systemic infection leading to poor tissue perfusion. Symptoms include hypotension, tachycardia, altered mental status, and elevated lactate indicating cellular hypoxia.


QUESTION 318
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptom is most characteristic of appendicitis?

OPTIONS:
A. Right lower quadrant abdominal pain
B. Severe flank pain
C. Epigastric burning
D. Left upper quadrant pain

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Appendicitis typically presents with pain in the right lower quadrant of the abdomen due to inflammation of the appendix.


QUESTION 319
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which virus most commonly causes bronchiolitis in infants?

OPTIONS:
A. Respiratory syncytial virus
B. Influenza virus
C. Adenovirus
D. Epstein-Barr virus

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Respiratory syncytial virus (RSV) is the leading cause of bronchiolitis in infants and young children and can lead to severe respiratory distress.


QUESTION 320
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A patient presents with fever, productive cough, shortness of breath, and crackles on lung auscultation.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Pneumonia
Asthma exacerbation
Pulmonary embolism

CORRECT CONDITION:
Pneumonia

INTERVENTIONS:
Administer antibiotics
Provide supplemental oxygen

MONITORING PARAMETER:
Oxygen saturation

RATIONALE:
The symptoms strongly indicate pneumonia, an infection of lung tissue. Antibiotics treat the infection, oxygen improves gas exchange, and oxygen saturation monitoring evaluates respiratory status.


QUESTION 321
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition involves infection of the kidney?

OPTIONS:
A. Pyelonephritis
B. Cystitis
C. Nephrolithiasis
D. Glomerulonephritis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Pyelonephritis is an infection affecting the kidney and renal pelvis, often presenting with flank pain, fever, and urinary symptoms.


QUESTION 322
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Heart Failure
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which findings indicate worsening heart failure?

OPTIONS:
A. Weight gain
B. Peripheral edema
C. Crackles in lungs
D. Shortness of breath
E. Increased appetite

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Heart failure leads to fluid retention causing weight gain, edema, pulmonary crackles, and dyspnea.


QUESTION 323
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes chronic airflow obstruction and destruction of alveoli?

OPTIONS:
A. Emphysema
B. Pneumonia
C. Bronchitis
D. Asthma

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Emphysema destroys alveolar walls, reducing surface area for gas exchange and causing chronic airflow limitation.


QUESTION 324
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which laboratory value requires immediate intervention?

OPTIONS:
A. Potassium 6.5 mmol/L
B. Sodium 138 mmol/L
C. Hemoglobin 12 g/dL
D. Glucose 110 mg/dL

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Severe hyperkalemia can cause life-threatening cardiac dysrhythmias and requires immediate treatment.


QUESTION 325
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication is classified as a beta blocker?

OPTIONS:
A. Metoprolol
B. Lisinopril
C. Amlodipine
D. Furosemide

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Metoprolol is a beta-adrenergic blocker used to treat hypertension, heart failure, and arrhythmias by slowing heart rate and reducing cardiac workload.


QUESTION 326
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Hypoxia
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptoms indicate hypoxia?

OPTIONS:
A. Restlessness
B. Cyanosis
C. Tachycardia
D. Confusion
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Hypoxia reduces oxygen delivery to tissues causing agitation, confusion, tachycardia, and cyanosis.


QUESTION 327
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes progressive degeneration of dopamine-producing neurons?

OPTIONS:
A. Parkinson disease
B. Alzheimer disease
C. Multiple sclerosis
D. Epilepsy

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Parkinson disease results from degeneration of dopaminergic neurons in the substantia nigra, causing tremor, rigidity, and slowed movement.


QUESTION 328
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition is characterized by hypertension and proteinuria during pregnancy?

OPTIONS:
A. Preeclampsia
B. Placenta previa
C. Gestational diabetes
D. Hyperemesis gravidarum

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Preeclampsia involves high blood pressure and proteinuria after 20 weeks of pregnancy and may progress to severe complications if untreated.


QUESTION 329
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Pulmonary Embolism
DIFFICULTY: hard

CASE:
A client presents with sudden shortness of breath, chest pain, and tachycardia.

QUESTION 1

STEM:
Which diagnostic test confirms pulmonary embolism?

OPTIONS:
A. CT pulmonary angiography
B. Chest x-ray
C. ECG
D. Spirometry

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
CT pulmonary angiography is the gold standard imaging study used to confirm pulmonary embolism.

QUESTION 2

STEM:
Which medication should the nurse anticipate administering?

OPTIONS:
A. Heparin
B. Insulin
C. Amoxicillin
D. Diazepam

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Heparin prevents further clot formation and is commonly used as an initial treatment for pulmonary embolism.


QUESTION 330
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Electrolytes
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which electrolyte imbalance causes muscle weakness and cardiac dysrhythmias?

OPTIONS:
A. Hyperkalemia
B. Hypernatremia
C. Hypermagnesemia
D. Hypophosphatemia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Elevated potassium levels interfere with cardiac electrical activity and neuromuscular function, leading to weakness and arrhythmias.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest database.

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be visible to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
They must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

IMPORT THE FOLLOWING RN QUESTIONS WITH RATIONALES INCLUDED


QUESTION 351
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which finding is most consistent with right-sided heart failure?

OPTIONS:
A. Peripheral edema
B. Pulmonary crackles
C. Orthopnea
D. Pink frothy sputum

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Right-sided heart failure causes systemic venous congestion leading to peripheral edema, hepatomegaly, and jugular venous distention. Pulmonary symptoms are more typical of left-sided failure.


QUESTION 352
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Myocardial Infarction
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptoms are commonly associated with myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS:
A. Chest pressure
B. Diaphoresis
C. Nausea
D. Shortness of breath
E. Increased appetite

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Myocardial infarction frequently presents with chest pressure, sweating, nausea, and dyspnea due to decreased cardiac perfusion and sympathetic activation.


QUESTION 353
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. Client with oxygen saturation 83%
B. Client with mild abdominal pain
C. Client requesting a blanket
D. Client with chronic arthritis pain

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
An oxygen saturation of 83% indicates severe hypoxemia and threatens oxygen delivery to tissues. Airway and breathing problems are always prioritized.


QUESTION 354
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which lung sound is most characteristic of asthma?

OPTIONS:
A. Wheezing
B. Crackles
C. Rhonchi
D. Pleural friction rub

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Asthma causes bronchoconstriction and airway narrowing which produces wheezing during expiration.


QUESTION 355
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Anaphylaxis
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Place the priority interventions for anaphylaxis in the correct order.

OPTIONS:
1 Administer epinephrine
2 Assess airway and breathing
3 Activate emergency response
4 Provide oxygen and IV access

CORRECT ORDER:
2
3
1
4

RATIONALE:
The nurse first assesses airway and breathing because airway compromise can rapidly become fatal. Emergency support is activated, epinephrine is administered, and oxygen and IV access are established.


QUESTION 356
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition results from rupture of a cerebral aneurysm?

OPTIONS:
A. Subarachnoid hemorrhage
B. Migraine
C. Multiple sclerosis
D. Parkinson disease

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Subarachnoid hemorrhage occurs when a cerebral aneurysm ruptures, causing bleeding into the subarachnoid space and sudden severe headache.


QUESTION 357
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Stroke
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptoms indicate possible stroke?

OPTIONS:
A. Facial droop
B. Arm weakness
C. Slurred speech
D. Sudden confusion
E. Increased appetite

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Stroke symptoms commonly include facial drooping, arm weakness, speech difficulty, and sudden confusion.


QUESTION 358
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which hormone increases blood glucose levels?

OPTIONS:
A. Glucagon
B. Insulin
C. Oxytocin
D. Melatonin

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Glucagon raises blood glucose by stimulating glycogen breakdown in the liver.


QUESTION 359
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptom is most associated with gallstones?

OPTIONS:
A. Right upper quadrant pain
B. Left lower quadrant pain
C. Severe headache
D. Hemoptysis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Gallstones commonly cause right upper quadrant abdominal pain, particularly after fatty meals.


QUESTION 360
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A client presents with fever, productive cough, and crackles on lung auscultation.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Pneumonia
Asthma
Pulmonary embolism

CORRECT CONDITION:
Pneumonia

INTERVENTIONS:
Administer antibiotics
Provide supplemental oxygen

MONITORING PARAMETER:
Oxygen saturation

RATIONALE:
These findings suggest pneumonia, a lung infection. Treatment includes antibiotics and oxygen therapy while monitoring oxygenation.


QUESTION 361
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition is characterized by kidney stones?

OPTIONS:
A. Nephrolithiasis
B. Pyelonephritis
C. Glomerulonephritis
D. Cystitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Nephrolithiasis refers to the formation of kidney stones which can cause severe flank pain and hematuria.


QUESTION 362
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Dehydration
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which signs indicate dehydration?

OPTIONS:
A. Dry mucous membranes
B. Decreased urine output
C. Tachycardia
D. Hypotension
E. Weight gain

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Dehydration causes reduced circulating volume leading to dry mucous membranes, decreased urine output, tachycardia, and hypotension.


QUESTION 363
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes a “whooping cough”?

OPTIONS:
A. Pertussis
B. RSV
C. Croup
D. Influenza

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Pertussis is a bacterial infection characterized by severe coughing fits followed by a distinctive “whooping” sound.


QUESTION 364
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which laboratory value requires immediate intervention?

OPTIONS:
A. Sodium 120 mmol/L
B. Sodium 138 mmol/L
C. Hemoglobin 12 g/dL
D. Glucose 110 mg/dL

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Severe hyponatremia can cause seizures, confusion, and cerebral edema and must be addressed urgently.


QUESTION 365
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication is used to treat bacterial infections?

OPTIONS:
A. Amoxicillin
B. Acyclovir
C. Fluconazole
D. Oseltamivir

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Amoxicillin is a beta-lactam antibiotic used to treat bacterial infections.


QUESTION 366
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Hypoglycemia
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which findings indicate hypoglycemia?

OPTIONS:
A. Sweating
B. Tremors
C. Confusion
D. Tachycardia
E. Hyperglycemia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Low blood glucose triggers adrenergic symptoms including sweating, tremors, tachycardia, and neurological symptoms such as confusion.


QUESTION 367
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which disorder causes progressive cognitive decline?

OPTIONS:
A. Alzheimer disease
B. Parkinson disease
C. ALS
D. Epilepsy

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Alzheimer disease is the most common cause of dementia characterized by progressive memory loss and cognitive impairment.


QUESTION 368
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes collapse of lung tissue?

OPTIONS:
A. Atelectasis
B. Asthma
C. Pneumonia
D. Bronchitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Atelectasis occurs when alveoli collapse, reducing gas exchange and oxygenation.


QUESTION 369
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Myocardial Infarction
DIFFICULTY: hard

CASE:
A patient presents with crushing chest pain radiating to the jaw and diaphoresis.

QUESTION 1

STEM:
Which diagnostic test confirms myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS:
A. Troponin
B. Glucose
C. Sodium
D. Potassium

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Troponin is the most specific biomarker for myocardial injury.

QUESTION 2

STEM:
Which medication should the nurse administer immediately?

OPTIONS:
A. Aspirin
B. Antibiotics
C. Insulin
D. Antihistamines

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Aspirin reduces platelet aggregation and improves coronary blood flow during myocardial infarction.


QUESTION 370
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which electrolyte imbalance causes peaked T waves on ECG?

OPTIONS:
A. Hyperkalemia
B. Hypokalemia
C. Hypercalcemia
D. Hyponatremia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Hyperkalemia alters cardiac conduction causing tall peaked T waves and arrhythmias.


QUESTION 371
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes inflammation of the colon?

OPTIONS:
A. Ulcerative colitis
B. Gastritis
C. Pancreatitis
D. Hepatitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Ulcerative colitis is an inflammatory bowel disease affecting the colon.


QUESTION 372
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which patient should be assessed first?

OPTIONS:
A. Respiratory rate 7 breaths/min
B. Temperature 37.5°C
C. Mild headache
D. Stable blood pressure

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A respiratory rate of 7 indicates severe hypoventilation and threatens oxygenation.


QUESTION 373
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication reverses opioid overdose?

OPTIONS:
A. Naloxone
B. Flumazenil
C. Diazepam
D. Atropine

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Naloxone is an opioid antagonist used to reverse respiratory depression from opioid overdose.


QUESTION 374
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which interventions are included in the sepsis bundle?

OPTIONS:
A. Obtain blood cultures
B. Administer broad spectrum antibiotics
C. Give IV fluids
D. Measure lactate
E. Delay treatment

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Early sepsis management includes blood cultures, IV fluids, antibiotics, and lactate measurement.


QUESTION 375
TYPE: bowtie

Ischemic stroke

MONITORING PARAMETER:
Neurological status

RATIONALE:
Rapid recognition and imaging are essential in stroke to determine treatment eligibility.
