SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

Upload the following questions to the NurseNest database.

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

IMPORTANT RULES

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
They must be visible to BOTH US RN and Canadian RN users.
They must NOT be placed in Respiratory Therapy (RT) content.
RT questions are uploaded separately.

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie


QUESTION 401
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which laboratory marker rises earliest after myocardial injury?

OPTIONS:
A. Troponin
B. Myoglobin
C. CK-MB
D. BNP

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Myoglobin rises within 1–3 hours after myocardial injury, making it the earliest marker, although it is less specific than troponin.


QUESTION 402
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Heart Failure
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which findings are consistent with left-sided heart failure?

OPTIONS:
A. Crackles in lungs
B. Dyspnea
C. Orthopnea
D. Pulmonary edema
E. Hepatomegaly

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Left-sided heart failure causes pulmonary congestion, resulting in crackles, dyspnea, orthopnea, and pulmonary edema. Hepatomegaly is more common in right-sided heart failure.


QUESTION 403
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. Client with new confusion and oxygen saturation 85%
B. Client requesting pain medication
C. Client with mild nausea
D. Client with constipation

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Altered mental status with hypoxia indicates inadequate oxygen delivery to the brain. Airway and breathing issues always take priority.


QUESTION 404
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes inflammation and narrowing of bronchioles in infants?

OPTIONS:
A. Bronchiolitis
B. Pneumonia
C. Asthma
D. Tuberculosis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Bronchiolitis is a viral infection (commonly RSV) causing inflammation of small airways in infants.


QUESTION 405
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: CPR
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Place the actions in the correct order when initiating adult CPR.

OPTIONS:
1 Start chest compressions  
2 Check responsiveness and breathing  
3 Activate emergency response system  
4 Attach AED  

CORRECT ORDER:
2
3
1
4

RATIONALE:
After confirming unresponsiveness, the nurse activates help, begins compressions, and applies an AED when available.


QUESTION 406
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which cranial nerve controls facial expression?

OPTIONS:
A. CN V
B. CN VII
C. CN VIII
D. CN X

CORRECT ANSWER:
B

RATIONALE:
Cranial nerve VII (facial nerve) controls muscles of facial expression.


QUESTION 407
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Stroke
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptoms are commonly seen in ischemic stroke?

OPTIONS:
A. Facial droop
B. Arm weakness
C. Speech difficulty
D. Sudden confusion
E. Severe itching

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Stroke commonly presents with FAST symptoms: facial droop, arm weakness, speech difficulty, and confusion.


QUESTION 408
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition results from excessive cortisol production?

OPTIONS:
A. Cushing syndrome
B. Addison disease
C. Hypothyroidism
D. Diabetes insipidus

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Cushing syndrome results from prolonged exposure to elevated cortisol levels.


QUESTION 409
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptom most strongly suggests pancreatitis?

OPTIONS:
A. Severe epigastric pain radiating to the back
B. Right lower quadrant pain
C. Painless jaundice
D. Flank pain

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Pancreatitis causes severe epigastric pain that frequently radiates to the back.


QUESTION 410
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A client presents with fever, dysuria, flank pain, and costovertebral tenderness.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Pyelonephritis
Cystitis
Nephrolithiasis

CORRECT CONDITION:
Pyelonephritis

INTERVENTIONS:
Administer antibiotics
Increase IV fluids

MONITORING PARAMETER:
Temperature

RATIONALE:
Flank pain and CVA tenderness strongly suggest kidney infection. Antibiotics treat infection while fluids support renal perfusion.


QUESTION 411
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which laboratory finding is most associated with renal failure?

OPTIONS:
A. Elevated creatinine
B. Decreased potassium
C. Low sodium
D. Elevated glucose

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Creatinine rises when kidneys lose the ability to filter waste products.


QUESTION 412
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Infection Control
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which precautions are required for tuberculosis?

OPTIONS:
A. Airborne precautions
B. Negative pressure room
C. N95 respirator
D. Limit patient transport
E. Contact precautions only

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Tuberculosis spreads via airborne particles and requires airborne isolation measures.


QUESTION 413
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which finding suggests dehydration in an infant?

OPTIONS:
A. Sunken fontanelle
B. Weight gain
C. Edema
D. Increased tears

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
A sunken fontanelle is a classic sign of dehydration in infants.


QUESTION 414
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which laboratory value requires immediate intervention?

OPTIONS:
A. Potassium 6.9 mmol/L
B. Sodium 140 mmol/L
C. Hemoglobin 13 g/dL
D. Glucose 110 mg/dL

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Severe hyperkalemia can cause lethal cardiac arrhythmias.


QUESTION 415
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication treats opioid overdose?

OPTIONS:
A. Naloxone
B. Flumazenil
C. Diazepam
D. Atropine

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Naloxone is an opioid antagonist that rapidly reverses respiratory depression caused by opioids.


QUESTION 416
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptoms indicate septic shock?

OPTIONS:
A. Hypotension
B. Tachycardia
C. Altered mental status
D. Elevated lactate
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Septic shock causes systemic hypoperfusion resulting in hypotension, tachycardia, confusion, and elevated lactate.


QUESTION 417
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which disorder is characterized by tremor, rigidity, and bradykinesia?

OPTIONS:
A. Parkinson disease
B. Alzheimer disease
C. Epilepsy
D. Stroke

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Parkinson disease results from dopamine depletion in the basal ganglia causing classic motor symptoms.


QUESTION 418
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes chronic airway obstruction and mucus production?

OPTIONS:
A. Chronic bronchitis
B. Pneumonia
C. Pulmonary fibrosis
D. Pleural effusion

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Chronic bronchitis is a COPD subtype characterized by productive cough and airway inflammation.


QUESTION 419
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Pulmonary Embolism
DIFFICULTY: hard

CASE:
A patient presents with sudden shortness of breath, chest pain, and tachycardia.

QUESTION 1

STEM:
Which diagnostic test confirms pulmonary embolism?

OPTIONS:
A. CT pulmonary angiography
B. Chest x-ray
C. ECG
D. Spirometry

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
CT pulmonary angiography is the most definitive diagnostic test for pulmonary embolism.

QUESTION 2

STEM:
Which medication should the nurse anticipate administering?

OPTIONS:
A. Heparin
B. Insulin
C. Amoxicillin
D. Diazepam

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Heparin prevents clot propagation and is the initial treatment for pulmonary embolism.


QUESTION 420
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Electrolytes
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which electrolyte imbalance commonly causes muscle weakness and arrhythmias?

OPTIONS:
A. Hyperkalemia
B. Hypernatremia
C. Hypercalcemia
D. Hypophosphatemia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Elevated potassium interferes with cardiac conduction and neuromuscular function.

QUESTION 451
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication is commonly used to treat acute pulmonary edema associated with heart failure?

OPTIONS:
A. Furosemide
B. Acetaminophen
C. Metformin
D. Amoxicillin

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Furosemide is a loop diuretic that removes excess fluid from the body, reducing pulmonary congestion and improving breathing in heart failure.


QUESTION 452
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Myocardial Infarction
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptoms may indicate myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS:
A. Chest pressure
B. Diaphoresis
C. Nausea
D. Shortness of breath
E. Increased appetite

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
MI commonly causes chest pressure, sweating, nausea, and dyspnea due to decreased coronary perfusion and sympathetic activation.


QUESTION 453
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS:
A. Client with oxygen saturation of 82%
B. Client requesting water
C. Client with mild headache
D. Client with constipation

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Severe hypoxemia threatens oxygen delivery to vital organs and requires immediate intervention.


QUESTION 454
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which disease is characterized by destruction of alveoli and air trapping?

OPTIONS:
A. Emphysema
B. Pneumonia
C. Asthma
D. Bronchitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Emphysema causes destruction of alveolar walls which reduces gas exchange and causes air trapping.


QUESTION 455
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Place the following sepsis interventions in order.

OPTIONS:
1 Obtain blood cultures  
2 Administer IV fluids  
3 Administer broad spectrum antibiotics  
4 Measure serum lactate  

CORRECT ORDER:
4
1
2
3

RATIONALE:
Early sepsis management includes measuring lactate to evaluate perfusion, obtaining cultures, initiating fluids to restore circulation, and administering antibiotics promptly.


QUESTION 456
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which disorder results from loss of dopamine-producing neurons?

OPTIONS:
A. Parkinson disease
B. Alzheimer disease
C. Multiple sclerosis
D. Epilepsy

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Parkinson disease occurs due to degeneration of dopamine-producing neurons in the substantia nigra.


QUESTION 457
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Stroke
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which findings suggest stroke?

OPTIONS:
A. Facial droop
B. Slurred speech
C. Arm weakness
D. Sudden confusion
E. Abdominal pain

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Stroke commonly causes neurologic deficits such as facial droop, speech difficulty, weakness, and confusion.


QUESTION 458
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which disorder results from insufficient insulin production?

OPTIONS:
A. Type 1 diabetes
B. Type 2 diabetes
C. Diabetes insipidus
D. Hyperthyroidism

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Type 1 diabetes results from autoimmune destruction of pancreatic beta cells leading to insulin deficiency.


QUESTION 459
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Gastrointestinal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition is characterized by inflammation of the appendix?

OPTIONS:
A. Appendicitis
B. Gastritis
C. Colitis
D. Pancreatitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Appendicitis causes inflammation of the appendix and typically presents with right lower quadrant pain.


QUESTION 460
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A client presents with sudden unilateral leg swelling and pain.

CONDITION OPTIONS:
Deep vein thrombosis
Pulmonary embolism
Cellulitis

CORRECT CONDITION:
Deep vein thrombosis

INTERVENTIONS:
Administer anticoagulants
Elevate the affected limb

MONITORING PARAMETER:
Signs of pulmonary embolism

RATIONALE:
DVT commonly causes unilateral leg swelling and pain. Treatment focuses on preventing clot propagation and monitoring for pulmonary embolism.


QUESTION 461
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which symptom is most associated with kidney stones?

OPTIONS:
A. Severe flank pain
B. Chest pain
C. Shortness of breath
D. Vision changes

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Kidney stones commonly cause severe flank pain that may radiate toward the groin.


QUESTION 462
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Infection Control
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which precautions are required for measles?

OPTIONS:
A. Airborne precautions
B. N95 respirator
C. Negative pressure room
D. Limit patient transport
E. Standard precautions only

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Measles spreads via airborne droplets and requires strict airborne isolation.


QUESTION 463
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes a barking cough and inspiratory stridor?

OPTIONS:
A. Croup
B. Pneumonia
C. Bronchitis
D. Asthma

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Croup causes upper airway inflammation resulting in a barking cough and stridor.


QUESTION 464
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which laboratory value requires immediate intervention?

OPTIONS:
A. Potassium 7.0 mmol/L
B. Sodium 140 mmol/L
C. Hemoglobin 13 g/dL
D. Glucose 105 mg/dL

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Severe hyperkalemia can cause life-threatening arrhythmias and requires urgent treatment.


QUESTION 465
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication class is used to treat hypertension by blocking angiotensin II receptors?

OPTIONS:
A. ARBs
B. Beta blockers
C. Calcium channel blockers
D. Loop diuretics

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Angiotensin receptor blockers prevent angiotensin II from causing vasoconstriction and fluid retention.


QUESTION 466
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Hypoxia
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which findings may indicate hypoxia?

OPTIONS:
A. Restlessness
B. Cyanosis
C. Tachycardia
D. Confusion
E. Bradycardia

CORRECT ANSWERS:
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE:
Hypoxia decreases oxygen delivery to tissues causing agitation, cyanosis, tachycardia, and confusion.


QUESTION 467
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which disorder causes progressive memory loss and dementia?

OPTIONS:
A. Alzheimer disease
B. Parkinson disease
C. Epilepsy
D. ALS

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Alzheimer disease is the most common cause of progressive dementia.


QUESTION 468
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition causes collapse of lung tissue?

OPTIONS:
A. Atelectasis
B. Asthma
C. Pneumonia
D. Bronchitis

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Atelectasis occurs when alveoli collapse leading to reduced oxygen exchange.


QUESTION 469
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Myocardial Infarction
DIFFICULTY: hard

CASE:
A patient presents with chest pain radiating to the jaw and diaphoresis.

QUESTION 1

STEM:
Which test confirms myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS:
A. Troponin
B. Sodium
C. Glucose
D. Potassium

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Troponin is the most specific biomarker for myocardial injury.

QUESTION 2

STEM:
Which medication should be given immediately?

OPTIONS:
A. Aspirin
B. Antibiotics
C. Insulin
D. Antihistamines

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Aspirin reduces platelet aggregation and improves coronary perfusion.


QUESTION 470
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Electrolytes
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which electrolyte imbalance causes muscle spasms and tetany?

OPTIONS:
A. Hypocalcemia
B. Hypernatremia
C. Hyperkalemia
D. Hypomagnesemia

CORRECT ANSWER:
A

RATIONALE:
Low calcium increases neuromuscular excitability causing tetany and spasms.

NURSENEST RN QUESTION BANK GENERATOR AND IMPORT PROMPT

Purpose
Populate the NurseNest RN question bank with a large set of exam-style questions aligned with both:

NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN licensing exam preparation

Content Tier
RN ONLY

These questions must NOT appear in:
Respiratory Therapy (RT)
RPN / LPN
NP

They must only appear in the RN tier.

Number of Questions
Generate questions 501 through 1000.

Distribution of Question Types

40% multiple choice
20% select all that apply
10% priority questions
10% ordered response
10% case study clusters
10% bowtie clinical judgment questions

All questions must include rationales.

Schema for Every Question

question_number
type
category
difficulty
target_exams
content_tier
stem
options
correct_answer_or_answers
rationale

NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

Uses concise exam-prep language

Example Question Format

QUESTION 501
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
Which medication is commonly administered first in suspected myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS
A Aspirin
B Acetaminophen
C Metformin
D Amoxicillin

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Aspirin inhibits platelet aggregation and reduces clot propagation in coronary arteries. Early administration improves survival in myocardial infarction.

Ensure realistic NCLEX-style wording.

Avoid repeating identical questions.

Ensure clinical accuracy.

Generate the entire RN question bank and prepare it for direct import into the NurseNest RN database.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

QUESTION 601
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A 68-year-old client arrives in the emergency department with crushing chest pain radiating to the left arm, diaphoresis, and nausea.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Acute myocardial infarction
Stable angina
Pericarditis

CORRECT CONDITION
Acute myocardial infarction

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer aspirin
Apply oxygen
Encourage ambulation
Delay ECG until labs return

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer aspirin
Apply oxygen

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Cardiac rhythm
Bowel sounds
Skin turgor
Peripheral pulses only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Cardiac rhythm

RATIONALE
The patient’s symptoms are classic for myocardial infarction. Early aspirin decreases platelet aggregation while oxygen improves myocardial oxygenation. Continuous cardiac monitoring detects dysrhythmias, which are a major cause of death following MI.


QUESTION 602
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A patient presents with sudden shortness of breath, chest pain, and tachycardia following prolonged immobilization after surgery.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Pulmonary embolism
Asthma exacerbation
Pneumonia

CORRECT CONDITION
Pulmonary embolism

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer anticoagulant therapy
Provide supplemental oxygen
Encourage vigorous exercise
Delay treatment until chest x-ray results

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer anticoagulant therapy
Provide supplemental oxygen

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Oxygen saturation
Bowel elimination
Blood glucose
Urine output only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Oxygen saturation

RATIONALE
Sudden dyspnea with tachycardia after immobility suggests pulmonary embolism. Oxygen improves oxygenation while anticoagulation prevents further clot formation. Oxygen saturation helps evaluate respiratory status.


QUESTION 603
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A client develops sudden facial droop, right arm weakness, and slurred speech.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Ischemic stroke
Migraine
Bell palsy

CORRECT CONDITION
Ischemic stroke

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Activate stroke protocol
Prepare for urgent brain imaging
Provide routine analgesics
Encourage sleep

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Activate stroke protocol
Prepare for urgent brain imaging

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Neurological status
Bowel sounds
Skin temperature
Urine color

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Neurological status

RATIONALE
FAST symptoms indicate acute stroke. Rapid protocol activation and CT imaging are required to determine eligibility for thrombolytic therapy. Ongoing neurological monitoring identifies deterioration.


QUESTION 604
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A patient with type 1 diabetes presents with hyperglycemia, dehydration, abdominal pain, and Kussmaul respirations.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Diabetic ketoacidosis
Hyperosmolar hyperglycemic state
Hypoglycemia

CORRECT CONDITION
Diabetic ketoacidosis

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer IV insulin
Provide IV fluids
Restrict fluids
Administer oral glucose

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer IV insulin
Provide IV fluids

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Serum potassium
Skin integrity
Visual acuity
Bowel movements

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Serum potassium

RATIONALE
DKA results from insulin deficiency leading to ketone production and metabolic acidosis. Treatment includes insulin and aggressive IV fluids. Potassium must be monitored because insulin shifts potassium into cells.


QUESTION 605
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A patient presents with fever, hypotension, tachycardia, and elevated lactate levels.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Septic shock
Hypovolemic shock
Cardiogenic shock

CORRECT CONDITION
Septic shock

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer broad spectrum antibiotics
Initiate IV fluid resuscitation
Delay treatment until cultures return
Encourage oral hydration only

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer broad spectrum antibiotics
Initiate IV fluid resuscitation

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Serum lactate
Skin turgor
Weight
Visual acuity

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Serum lactate

RATIONALE
Septic shock results from systemic infection causing severe hypotension and tissue hypoperfusion. Early antibiotics and fluid resuscitation are essential. Lactate levels indicate severity of tissue hypoxia.


QUESTION 606
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A patient presents with severe flank pain radiating to the groin and hematuria.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Nephrolithiasis
Pyelonephritis
Glomerulonephritis

CORRECT CONDITION
Nephrolithiasis

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer pain medication
Encourage increased fluid intake
Restrict fluids
Administer insulin

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer pain medication
Encourage increased fluid intake

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Urine output
Skin temperature
Respiratory rate
Hearing ability

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Urine output

RATIONALE
Kidney stones commonly cause severe flank pain and hematuria. Management includes pain control and hydration to help pass the stone. Urine output monitoring ensures adequate renal function.


QUESTION 607
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A patient suddenly develops absent breath sounds on one side of the chest, hypotension, and tracheal deviation after trauma.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Tension pneumothorax
Pleural effusion
Asthma exacerbation

CORRECT CONDITION
Tension pneumothorax

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Provide high flow oxygen
Prepare for needle decompression
Encourage coughing
Delay treatment

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Provide high flow oxygen
Prepare for needle decompression

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Respiratory status
Bowel movements
Blood glucose
Vision changes

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Respiratory status

RATIONALE
Tension pneumothorax is a life-threatening condition where air accumulates in the pleural space causing lung collapse and mediastinal shift. Immediate oxygen and decompression are required. Respiratory status must be monitored closely.


QUESTION 608
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Obstetrics
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
A pregnant client at 34 weeks presents with hypertension, proteinuria, and severe headache.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Preeclampsia
Placenta previa
Gestational diabetes

CORRECT CONDITION
Preeclampsia

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer magnesium sulfate
Monitor blood pressure
Encourage dehydration
Delay treatment

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer magnesium sulfate
Monitor blood pressure

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Neurological status
Hearing ability
Skin temperature
Bowel elimination

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Neurological status

RATIONALE
Preeclampsia involves hypertension and organ dysfunction during pregnancy. Magnesium sulfate prevents seizures while blood pressure monitoring prevents complications such as stroke.

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

These questions belong ONLY to RN content.
Do NOT place them in RT, RPN/LPN, or NP content.

SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPES

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie


QUESTION 701
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication is classified as an ACE inhibitor?

OPTIONS
A Lisinopril
B Metoprolol
C Amlodipine
D Furosemide

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Lisinopril is an ACE inhibitor that lowers blood pressure by blocking conversion of angiotensin I to angiotensin II.


QUESTION 702
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medication is used to reverse benzodiazepine overdose?

OPTIONS
A Naloxone
B Flumazenil
C Atropine
D Epinephrine

CORRECT ANSWER
B

RATIONALE
Flumazenil is a benzodiazepine antagonist used to reverse sedation caused by benzodiazepines.


QUESTION 703
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Pharmacology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which medications are beta blockers?

OPTIONS
A Metoprolol
B Atenolol
C Propranolol
D Lisinopril
E Losartan

CORRECT ANSWERS
A
B
C

RATIONALE
Beta blockers reduce heart rate and cardiac workload by blocking beta-adrenergic receptors.


QUESTION 704
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Leadership
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which client should the nurse assess first?

OPTIONS
A Client with sudden chest pain and diaphoresis
B Client requesting sleep medication
C Client with mild nausea
D Client waiting for discharge instructions

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Chest pain with diaphoresis suggests myocardial infarction and requires immediate assessment.


QUESTION 705
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Delegation
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which task can the RN safely delegate to a nursing assistant?

OPTIONS
A Assisting a stable patient with bathing
B Administering IV medication
C Assessing lung sounds
D Teaching a patient about medications

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Nursing assistants may perform basic care tasks for stable patients. Assessment and medication administration must be performed by licensed nurses.


QUESTION 706
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which finding is most concerning in a patient with increased intracranial pressure?

OPTIONS
A Unequal pupils
B Mild headache
C Temperature 37.4°C
D Pulse 80 bpm

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Unequal pupils may indicate brain herniation due to increased intracranial pressure and requires urgent intervention.


QUESTION 707
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM:
Which findings are associated with increased intracranial pressure?

OPTIONS
A Altered consciousness
B Vomiting
C Pupillary changes
D Bradycardia
E Increased appetite

CORRECT ANSWERS
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE
ICP causes neurologic deterioration including altered LOC, vomiting, pupillary changes, and Cushing’s reflex.


QUESTION 708
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which condition is characterized by hypertension and proteinuria during pregnancy?

OPTIONS
A Preeclampsia
B Placenta previa
C Gestational diabetes
D Hyperemesis gravidarum

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Preeclampsia occurs after 20 weeks of pregnancy and involves hypertension and organ dysfunction.


QUESTION 709
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which infection most commonly causes bronchiolitis in infants?

OPTIONS
A Respiratory syncytial virus
B Influenza virus
C Adenovirus
D Epstein-Barr virus

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
RSV is the most common cause of bronchiolitis and lower respiratory infections in infants.


QUESTION 710
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM:
Which sign indicates dehydration in infants?

OPTIONS
A Sunken fontanelle
B Increased tears
C Weight gain
D Edema

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
A sunken fontanelle indicates decreased fluid volume in infants.


QUESTION 711
TYPE: case_study
CATEGORY: Next Generation NCLEX
DIFFICULTY: hard

CASE
A 70-year-old patient presents with sudden weakness on the right side and difficulty speaking.

QUESTION 1

TYPE multiple_choice

STEM
Which condition is most likely?

OPTIONS
A Ischemic stroke
B Migraine
C Bell palsy
D Epilepsy

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Sudden neurological deficits such as weakness and speech difficulty indicate stroke.


QUESTION 2

TYPE select_all_that_apply

STEM
Which immediate interventions are appropriate?

OPTIONS
A Activate stroke protocol
B Obtain CT scan
C Administer thrombolytics if eligible
D Encourage ambulation
E Delay imaging

CORRECT ANSWERS
A
B
C

RATIONALE
Rapid stroke protocol activation and imaging determine eligibility for thrombolytic therapy.


QUESTION 712
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Clinical Judgment
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM
A patient presents with fever, productive cough, and crackles.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Pneumonia
Asthma
Pulmonary embolism

CORRECT CONDITION
Pneumonia

INTERVENTIONS
Administer antibiotics
Provide oxygen

MONITORING PARAMETER
Oxygen saturation

RATIONALE
Pneumonia is an infection of lung tissue causing cough, fever, and crackles.


QUESTION 713
TYPE: ordered_response
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM
Place the steps for managing anaphylaxis in order.

OPTIONS
1 Administer epinephrine
2 Assess airway
3 Call emergency response
4 Provide oxygen

CORRECT ORDER
2
3
1
4

RATIONALE
Airway must be assessed first, emergency help activated, epinephrine administered, and oxygen provided.


QUESTION 714
TYPE: select_all_that_apply
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM
Which interventions are part of the sepsis bundle?

OPTIONS
A Blood cultures
B IV antibiotics
C IV fluids
D Lactate measurement
E Delay treatment

CORRECT ANSWERS
A
B
C
D

RATIONALE
Early sepsis treatment includes cultures, antibiotics, fluids, and lactate monitoring.


QUESTION 715
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM
Which electrolyte abnormality produces peaked T waves on ECG?

OPTIONS
A Hyperkalemia
B Hypokalemia
C Hyponatremia
D Hypercalcemia

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Hyperkalemia causes tall peaked T waves and life-threatening arrhythmias.


QUESTION 716
TYPE: priority
CATEGORY: Critical Care
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM
Which patient requires immediate intervention?

OPTIONS
A Respiratory rate 8/min
B Mild headache
C Temperature 37.6°C
D Stable blood pressure

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Severe hypoventilation threatens oxygenation and requires urgent intervention.


QUESTION 717
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM
Which condition involves infection of the kidney?

OPTIONS
A Pyelonephritis
B Cystitis
C Nephrolithiasis
D Glomerulonephritis

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Pyelonephritis is an upper urinary tract infection affecting the kidneys.


QUESTION 718
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM
Which condition causes collapse of alveoli?

OPTIONS
A Atelectasis
B Asthma
C Pneumonia
D Bronchitis

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Atelectasis occurs when alveoli collapse and cannot participate in gas exchange.


QUESTION 719
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: moderate

STEM
Which disease causes progressive degeneration of dopamine-producing neurons?

OPTIONS
A Parkinson disease
B Alzheimer disease
C Multiple sclerosis
D Epilepsy

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Parkinson disease results from loss of dopaminergic neurons in the substantia nigra.


QUESTION 720
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Emergency
DIFFICULTY: hard

STEM
A trauma patient develops tracheal deviation and absent breath sounds on one side.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Tension pneumothorax
Pleural effusion
Asthma

CORRECT CONDITION
Tension pneumothorax

INTERVENTIONS
Provide high flow oxygen
Prepare for needle decompression

MONITORING PARAMETER
Respiratory status

RATIONALE
Tension pneumothorax causes lung collapse and mediastinal shift requiring immediate decompression.

NURSENEST RN MEGA QUESTION BANK GENERATOR AND IMPORT PROMPT

Purpose
Populate the NurseNest RN question bank with a large set of exam-style questions aligned with both:

NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN licensing exam preparation

Content Tier
RN ONLY

These questions must NOT appear in:
Respiratory Therapy (RT)
RPN / LPN
NP

They must only appear in the RN tier.

Number of Questions
Generate questions 1001 through 2000.

Distribution of Question Types

40 percent multiple choice
20 percent select all that apply
10 percent priority questions
10 percent ordered response
10 percent case study clusters
10 percent bowtie clinical judgment questions

All questions must include rationales.

Schema for Every Question

question_number
type
category
difficulty
target_exams
content_tier
stem
options
correct_answer_or_answers_or_order
rationale

Target Exams

NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

Content Tier

RN

Difficulty Distribution

30 percent moderate
40 percent hard
30 percent very hard

Clinical Categories to Cover

Cardiac
Respiratory
Endocrine
Neurology
Gastrointestinal
Renal
Electrolytes
Pharmacology
Maternal health
Pediatrics
Mental health
Infection control
Sepsis
Emergency nursing
Critical care
Leadership and delegation
Ethics
Patient safety

Pharmacology Requirements

Include medications from these classes:

ACE inhibitors
ARBs
Beta blockers
Calcium channel blockers
Loop diuretics
Thiazide diuretics
Anticoagulants
Antiplatelets
Antibiotics
Insulin and diabetic agents
Opioids
Antidotes
Sedatives
Antipsychotics

Next Generation NCLEX Case Clusters

Include complex multi-question case studies where a clinical scenario is followed by 2 to 4 related questions.

Example format

CASE STUDY

Patient description

QUESTION A
TYPE: multiple_choice

QUESTION B
TYPE: select_all_that_apply

QUESTION C
TYPE: priority

QUESTION D
TYPE: ordered_response

Bowtie Questions

Structure:

SCENARIO

Condition options
Correct condition

Intervention options
Two correct interventions

Monitoring parameter options
One correct monitoring parameter

Every bowtie question must include rationale explaining clinical reasoning.

Priority Questions

Use these frameworks:

Airway Breathing Circulation
Acute versus chronic
Stable versus unstable
Safety risk
Maslow physiological needs

Select All That Apply

Use 4 to 6 options
Include 2 to 4 correct answers

Ordered Response Examples

Stroke protocol
Sepsis bundle
Trauma assessment
CPR steps
Emergency medication sequence
Post-operative complications management

Rationales

Every question must include a rationale that:

Explains why the correct answer is correct
Includes key clinical reasoning
Uses concise exam preparation language
References core nursing physiology or safety principles

Example Output Format

QUESTION 1001
TYPE: multiple_choice
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: moderate
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM
Which medication is commonly administered first in suspected myocardial infarction?

OPTIONS
A Aspirin
B Acetaminophen
C Metformin
D Amoxicillin

CORRECT ANSWER
A

RATIONALE
Aspirin inhibits platelet aggregation and reduces clot formation in coronary arteries. Early administration improves survival in myocardial infarction.

Output Requirements

Generate questions sequentially from 1001 through 2000.

Every question must follow the schema exactly.

Include rationales for every question.

Ensure realistic NCLEX-style wording.

Avoid repeating identical questions.

Ensure clinical accuracy.

Final Instruction

Generate the entire RN mega question bank and prepare it for direct import into the NurseNest RN database.

NURSENEST NCLEX EXAM SIMULATOR UI MASTER PROMPT

Build a production-ready RN exam simulator for NurseNest that closely mirrors the experience of the real NCLEX style testing environment while remaining original in branding and implementation.

PRIMARY GOAL

Create a polished, responsive, high-conversion exam simulator UI for the RN tier that supports both:

NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

This simulator must be used ONLY for RN content.
It must NOT display RT, RPN/LPN, or NP questions.

CONTENT TIER RULES

Only load questions where:
content_tier = RN

Only show exams tagged:
US RN
Canadian RN

Do not mix in:
Respiratory Therapy
RPN
LPN
NP

PRODUCT GOAL

The simulator should feel premium, modern, calm, clinically clean, and psychologically reassuring.
It should make learners feel:
focused
supported
challenged
prepared
confident

VISUAL STYLE

Use the NurseNest brand style:
soft, modern clinical look
rounded corners
gentle shadows
clean white cards
pastel accents
feminine but professional
minimal clutter
excellent spacing
calm exam environment

Suggested design direction:
off-white background
soft lilac or pastel blue accent
rounded buttons
sticky top progress bar
clear exam timer
subtle hover states
large readable font
mobile-friendly but optimized for desktop exam use

DO NOT copy Pearson VUE branding or proprietary layouts exactly.
The interface should feel familiar in function, not duplicated in appearance.

TECH STACK

Use the current NurseNest stack.
Assume:
React
TypeScript or JavaScript
Vite
Wouter if routing is needed
Tailwind if available
Existing NurseNest authentication and role system
Existing admin question bank and exam data models

CORE FEATURES REQUIRED

1. Exam Selection Screen

Create an RN exam selection page that allows the learner to choose:
exam mode
question count
difficulty
system category
timed vs untimed
US RN vs Canadian RN focus
mixed exam vs body-system exam
NGN only mode
pharmacology only mode
priority and delegation only mode

Exam modes:
Quick Practice
Full Exam
Custom Quiz
NGN Case Practice
Bowtie Practice
Pharmacology Drill
Priority and Delegation Drill
Wrong Answers Retry
Saved for Review Retry

2. Exam Engine

Build the actual exam-taking experience with:
one question visible at a time
previous button
next button
flag for review
clear but safe exit warning
question number navigator
unanswered / answered / flagged states
timer
progress tracker
pause only in practice mode, not in strict exam simulation mode
auto-save progress
resume exam if page reloads

3. Question Types Supported

The engine must render these question types correctly:

multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

4. Multiple Choice UI

Display:
question stem
4 or more answer options
single selection only
clear selected state
optional rationale only after submission in practice mode
no rationale during real exam simulation mode

5. SATA UI

Display:
question stem
checkbox-based options
allow multiple selections
prevent submission until at least one answer is chosen
show partial-cognitive realism but scoring should follow backend rules

6. Ordered Response UI

Display:
draggable ranked answer list
keyboard-accessible reorder controls
clear numbering
reset ordering button

Use for:
stroke protocol
CPR
sepsis sequence
emergency priorities
trauma workflow

7. Case Study UI

Build a multi-panel layout for NGN case studies.

Required structure:
left panel or top panel with patient scenario
tabs or sections for:
history
vitals
labs
provider notes
medications
nursing notes

right panel or main panel with question set tied to the case

Case study questions may include:
multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response

The learner must be able to move between questions in the same case without losing responses.

8. Bowtie UI

Build an NGN bowtie interface with three sections:

Section 1:
Select the most likely condition

Section 2:
Select two appropriate interventions

Section 3:
Select the most important parameter to monitor

Requirements:
clean card-based layout
single select for condition
multi-select with max 2 for interventions
single select for monitoring parameter
validation before submit
clear visual grouping
easy on desktop and tablet

9. Exam Navigation

Create a question navigator grid that shows:
answered questions
unanswered questions
flagged questions
current question

Use color states and labels.
Allow direct jump to a question in practice mode.
In strict simulation mode, allow navigation consistent with chosen exam mode settings.

10. Timer and Exam Controls

Top bar should include:
exam title
timer
progress
question number
mode label

Modes:
Practice Mode
Simulation Mode
Tutor Mode

Practice Mode:
rationale after each question optional
pause allowed
review allowed

Simulation Mode:
no rationale until end
timer required
limited interruptions
exam-like pressure

Tutor Mode:
instant explanations
show learning objective
show category tag

11. Review Screen

After submission, show:
score
percent correct
performance by category
performance by question type
time spent
flagged questions review
incorrect questions review
correct answer and full rationale
study recommendations

12. Rationales

Rationales are extremely important.
The UI must support:
full rationale display
why the correct answer is correct
optionally why distractors are incorrect if backend provides it
highlighted takeaway box
clinical pearl area if available

13. Learning Analytics

Track:
question accuracy
time per question
topic weakness
most-missed categories
NGN performance
bowtie performance
pharmacology performance
trend over time

Display:
strengths
weaknesses
recommended next quiz
readiness estimate

14. Admin Compatibility

The UI must work with question objects that include fields like:

question_number
type
category
difficulty
target_exams
content_tier
stem
options
correct_answer_or_answers_or_order
rationale

For case studies also support:
case_text
case_tabs
linked_questions

For bowtie also support:
condition_options
correct_condition
intervention_options
correct_interventions
monitoring_parameter_options
correct_monitoring_parameter

15. Data Validation

Only render questions when:
content_tier = RN

Filter exam pools by:
US RN
Canadian RN
or both

Prevent accidental loading of RT questions.
If a non-RN question appears, exclude it and log a warning in admin/debug mode.

16. Exam Scoring

Support:
raw score
percentage
question type breakdown
category breakdown
flagged review summary

For NGN formats, structure scoring so backend can later support:
all-or-nothing
partial credit
weighted scoring

Do not hardcode simplistic scoring assumptions that would block later upgrades.

17. Accessibility

Must include:
keyboard navigation
visible focus states
high contrast text
draggable alternatives for ordered response
screen-reader-friendly labels
clear error states
large click targets

18. Mobile and Desktop

Desktop should be primary because this is an exam simulator.
Mobile should still be fully functional.
Case studies should collapse elegantly on smaller screens.
Bowtie sections should stack vertically on mobile.

19. Psychological Design

This exam simulator should reduce panic and improve retention.
Add:
clean spacing
encouraging microcopy
non-distracting progress feedback
clear reassurance when answers are saved
subtle confidence-building language

Examples:
Answer saved
You can review flagged items later
Stay focused, one question at a time

Do not overdo this. Keep it professional.

20. Results Recommendation Engine

After the exam, recommend next actions such as:
retry flagged questions
pharmacology drill
cardiac remediation
NGN case practice
priority and delegation set

Recommendations should be based on actual weak categories.

21. Pages / Components to Build

Build these screens and components:

RNExamDashboard
RNExamSetupModal or page
RNExamPlayer
RNQuestionCard
RNSATAQuestion
RNOrderedResponseQuestion
RNCaseStudyRenderer
RNBowtieRenderer
RNExamTopBar
RNQuestionNavigator
RNExamResults
RNReviewMode
RNPerformanceBreakdown
RNWeaknessRecommendations

22. Suggested State Model

Track:
currentExam
questions
currentQuestionIndex
responses
flaggedQuestions
timeRemaining
examMode
isSubmitted
reviewMode
results
categoryPerformance
questionTypePerformance

23. Suggested UX Details

Warn before leaving unfinished exam
Autosave every answer
Persist to local storage and backend
Allow resume from interruption
Show confirmation when exam submitted
Show incomplete question count before final submit

24. Import / Backend Requirements

Ensure simulator can consume RN question bank entries already created for NurseNest.
Build parsing logic for:
multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

25. Monetization / Product Logic

Support role-based gating:
free user sees limited exam set
paid RN user sees full RN bank
premium user sees NGN case clusters, analytics, and custom exams

Create upgrade prompts that are tasteful, not spammy.
Examples:
Unlock full NGN case practice
Access advanced analytics with RN Premium

26. Deliverables Required

Generate:
complete frontend component structure
state management plan
sample exam player code
sample bowtie renderer code
sample case study renderer code
sample results page code
responsive layout
clean Tailwind styling
import-ready mock RN question dataset examples
clear instructions for wiring to existing NurseNest backend

27. Sample Question Object Support

The simulator must support objects like:

{
  "question_number": 601,
  "type": "bowtie",
  "category": "Cardiac",
  "difficulty": "hard",
  "target_exams": ["US RN", "Canadian RN"],
  "content_tier": "RN",

CONTENT_TIER: RN

QUESTION 609
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with a history of heart failure presents with severe dyspnea, crackles, pink frothy sputum, and oxygen saturation of 82%.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Acute pulmonary edema
Pulmonary embolism
Asthma exacerbation

CORRECT CONDITION
Acute pulmonary edema

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer oxygen
Prepare to give IV diuretic
Encourage large oral fluid intake
Place the client flat in bed

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer oxygen
Prepare to give IV diuretic

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Respiratory status
Bowel sounds
Visual acuity
Skin temperature

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Respiratory status

RATIONALE
Pink frothy sputum, crackles, and severe hypoxemia in a client with heart failure strongly suggest acute pulmonary edema. Oxygen supports gas exchange and IV diuretics reduce fluid overload. Respiratory status must be monitored closely because deterioration can occur quickly.

QUESTION 610
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with chest discomfort that occurs with exertion and resolves with rest.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Stable angina
Myocardial infarction
Aortic dissection

CORRECT CONDITION
Stable angina

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Reduce activity
Administer antianginal therapy as prescribed
Prepare for immediate thrombolysis
Encourage strenuous exercise

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Reduce activity
Administer antianginal therapy as prescribed

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Chest pain response
Bowel elimination
Hearing changes
Urine color

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Chest pain response

RATIONALE
Stable angina is triggered by exertion and relieved by rest. Activity reduction lowers myocardial oxygen demand, and antianginal therapy improves coronary perfusion. Monitoring pain response helps determine if symptoms are improving or worsening.

QUESTION 611
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with sudden onset of the worst headache of their life, photophobia, vomiting, and nuchal rigidity.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Subarachnoid hemorrhage
Migraine
Meningitis

CORRECT CONDITION
Subarachnoid hemorrhage

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Prepare for urgent neuroimaging
Maintain close neurologic monitoring
Encourage ambulation
Delay evaluation until pain improves

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Prepare for urgent neuroimaging
Maintain close neurologic monitoring

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Level of consciousness
Bowel sounds
Capillary refill
Oral intake

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Level of consciousness

RATIONALE
A thunderclap headache with meningeal irritation signs strongly suggests subarachnoid hemorrhage. Immediate neuroimaging and close neurologic monitoring are essential because deterioration can be rapid and life-threatening.

QUESTION 612
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with epilepsy is actively seizing for more than 5 minutes.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Status epilepticus
Transient ischemic attack
Syncope

CORRECT CONDITION
Status epilepticus

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Protect the airway
Prepare to administer anticonvulsant therapy
Place an object in the mouth
Restrain the client firmly

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Protect the airway
Prepare to administer anticonvulsant therapy

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Oxygenation status
Bowel habits
Skin moisture
Peripheral edema

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Oxygenation status

RATIONALE
A seizure lasting more than 5 minutes is status epilepticus and is a medical emergency. Airway protection and rapid anticonvulsant treatment are priorities. Oxygenation must be monitored because hypoxia is a major risk during prolonged seizures.

QUESTION 613
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with diabetes is diaphoretic, confused, shaky, and has a bedside glucose of 2.8 mmol/L.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Hypoglycemia
Diabetic ketoacidosis
Hyperosmolar hyperglycemic state

CORRECT CONDITION
Hypoglycemia

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Provide rapid-acting carbohydrate if safe to swallow
Recheck glucose after treatment
Restrict oral intake
Administer long-acting insulin immediately

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Provide rapid-acting carbohydrate if safe to swallow
Recheck glucose after treatment

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Blood glucose
Bowel sounds
Urine specific gravity
Visual acuity

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Blood glucose

RATIONALE
Diaphoresis, tremor, confusion, and a glucose of 2.8 mmol/L indicate hypoglycemia. Rapid carbohydrate corrects the low glucose if the client can swallow safely, and repeat glucose testing confirms response to treatment.

QUESTION 614
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Endocrine
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with weight loss, heat intolerance, tachycardia, anxiety, and tremor.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Hyperthyroidism
Hypothyroidism
Addison disease

CORRECT CONDITION
Hyperthyroidism

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Monitor heart rate
Administer antithyroid therapy as prescribed
Apply warming blankets
Encourage large iodine supplements without evaluation

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Monitor heart rate
Administer antithyroid therapy as prescribed

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Cardiac status
Urine ketones
Bowel sounds only
Skin turgor

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Cardiac status

RATIONALE
These findings are classic for hyperthyroidism. Tachycardia and increased metabolic rate can place strain on the cardiovascular system, so cardiac monitoring and prescribed antithyroid therapy are appropriate priorities.

QUESTION 615
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with asthma has severe wheezing, chest tightness, accessory muscle use, and difficulty speaking in full sentences.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Acute asthma exacerbation
Pleural effusion
Pulmonary edema

CORRECT CONDITION
Acute asthma exacerbation

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer bronchodilator therapy
Provide supplemental oxygen
Encourage smoke exposure avoidance later only
Delay treatment while awaiting spirometry

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer bronchodilator therapy
Provide supplemental oxygen

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Respiratory effort
Bowel elimination
Peripheral edema
Urine output

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Respiratory effort

RATIONALE
Severe wheezing with accessory muscle use and inability to speak full sentences indicates significant asthma exacerbation. Rapid bronchodilation and oxygen are needed, and respiratory effort must be monitored for worsening fatigue or impending failure.

QUESTION 616
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A postoperative client develops sudden dyspnea, pleuritic chest pain, tachycardia, and low oxygen saturation.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Pulmonary embolism
Pneumonia
Atelectasis

CORRECT CONDITION
Pulmonary embolism

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Apply oxygen
Prepare for anticoagulation as prescribed
Encourage unassisted ambulation immediately
Delay evaluation until morning rounds

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Apply oxygen
Prepare for anticoagulation as prescribed

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Oxygen saturation
Bowel sounds
Blood glucose
Skin integrity

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Oxygen saturation

RATIONALE
Sudden dyspnea with pleuritic chest pain and tachycardia after surgery is highly suspicious for pulmonary embolism. Oxygen supports gas exchange and anticoagulation is standard treatment to prevent clot extension.

QUESTION 617
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

A client has fever, flank pain, dysuria, and costovertebral angle tenderness.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Pyelonephritis
Cystitis
Nephrotic syndrome

CORRECT CONDITION
Pyelonephritis

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer prescribed antibiotics
Encourage hydration as appropriate
Restrict all fluids
Delay urine testing

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer prescribed antibiotics
Encourage hydration as appropriate

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Temperature
Bowel sounds
Vision
Peripheral pulses

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Temperature

RATIONALE
Fever, flank pain, dysuria, and CVA tenderness indicate pyelonephritis. Antibiotics treat the infection, hydration supports urinary clearance, and temperature monitoring helps assess response to treatment.

QUESTION 618
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Renal
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with renal failure develops muscle weakness and an ECG showing peaked T waves.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Hyperkalemia
Hypokalemia
Hypercalcemia

CORRECT CONDITION
Hyperkalemia

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Place on cardiac monitoring
Prepare potassium-lowering treatment
Give potassium supplements
Encourage high-potassium foods

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Place on cardiac monitoring
Prepare potassium-lowering treatment

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Cardiac rhythm
Bowel elimination
Skin color
Visual acuity

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Cardiac rhythm

RATIONALE
Muscle weakness with peaked T waves is classic for hyperkalemia, especially in renal failure. The immediate risk is life-threatening dysrhythmia, so cardiac monitoring and potassium-lowering therapy are priorities.

QUESTION 619
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A postpartum client is saturating a perineal pad every 15 minutes and reports dizziness.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Postpartum hemorrhage
Expected lochia
Endometritis

CORRECT CONDITION
Postpartum hemorrhage

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Assess fundal tone
Prepare for rapid fluid replacement
Encourage ambulation to the bathroom alone
Delay reassessment for one hour

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Assess fundal tone
Prepare for rapid fluid replacement

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Hemodynamic status
Bowel function
Visual acuity
Hearing

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Hemodynamic status

RATIONALE
Heavy bleeding with dizziness postpartum suggests hemorrhage and possible hypovolemia. Fundal assessment helps identify uterine atony, and rapid fluid support may be needed. Hemodynamic monitoring is essential to detect instability.

QUESTION 620
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
An infant has a barking cough, inspiratory stridor, and hoarse cry.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Croup
Epiglottitis
Bronchiolitis

CORRECT CONDITION
Croup

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Provide humidified oxygen as needed
Keep the child calm
Perform repeated throat inspection with a tongue depressor
Force oral fluids immediately during distress

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Provide humidified oxygen as needed
Keep the child calm

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Work of breathing
Bowel elimination
Urine glucose
Skin turgor only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Work of breathing

RATIONALE
A barking cough with stridor and hoarseness is typical of croup. Keeping the child calm helps avoid worsening airway obstruction, and oxygen may be needed if respiratory effort increases. Work of breathing is the key monitoring priority.

  "title": "COPD Exacerbation on Mechanical Ventilation",

  "difficulty": "medium",

    "questions": [
      {
        "external_id": "caseq_001",
        "stem": "What is the primary acid-base disorder?",
        "options": {
          "A": "Respiratory acidosis",
          "B": "Metabolic acidosis",
          "C": "Respiratory alkalosis",
          "D": "Metabolic alkalosis"
        },
        "correct_answer": "A",
        "rationale": "The pH is low and PaCO2 is elevated, indicating respiratory acidosis."
      },
      {
        "external_id": "caseq_002",
        "stem": "Which ventilator adjustment would most directly help lower the PaCO2?",
        "options": {
          "A": "Increase respiratory rate",

NURSENEST RN EXAM SIMULATOR + ADMIN IMPORT + LIVE PUBLISH MASTER PROMPT

Build a production-ready RN exam system for NurseNest that does all of the following in one connected workflow:

1. Allows admin to upload RN questions into the database
2. Validates and stores those RN questions correctly
3. Publishes those RN questions to the live site immediately after import
4. Makes the RN questions available inside the RN exam simulator
5. Keeps RN content completely separate from RT, RPN/LPN, and NP content
6. Supports both US NCLEX-RN and Canadian RN exam preparation
7. Supports all major NCLEX and Next Generation NCLEX style question types
8. Displays rationales correctly in practice and review modes
9. Uses role-based access so only the correct users can access the correct RN content

OVERALL GOAL

Create a clean, scalable, premium RN exam platform for NurseNest that feels modern, trustworthy, calm, and academically rigorous.

This system must support:
RN admin upload
RN live publishing
RN exam generation
RN exam simulation
RN results analytics
RN review mode
RN rationale display
RN filtering by US RN and Canadian RN

IMPORTANT CONTENT RULES

Only RN content is handled by this system.

Strictly allow only:
content_tier = RN

Allow target exams:
US RN
Canadian RN

Do NOT allow any upload, rendering, indexing, or display of:
Respiratory Therapy
RT
RPN
LPN
NP

If any uploaded record is not RN, reject it or quarantine it in admin review mode.

PART 1: ADMIN IMPORT WORKFLOW

Build an RN Admin Import page and backend workflow.

Required admin features:
drag and drop upload
paste raw question blocks
bulk text import
JSON import
preview before import
validation errors display
duplicate detection
publish toggle
draft toggle
category assignment
difficulty assignment
target exam assignment
question type recognition
rationale validation
live publish action

Admin page name:
RNQuestionImportAdmin

Admin workflow:
1. Admin pastes or uploads question content
2. System parses questions into structured RN records
3. System validates required fields
4. System previews parsed questions
5. Admin approves import
6. System stores records in RN question bank
7. System marks approved questions as published
8. Published questions appear on the live site immediately
9. Questions become available in RN exam generator and RN simulator without needing manual redeploy

PART 2: REQUIRED QUESTION FIELDS

Every RN question record must support:

id
question_number
type
category
difficulty
target_exams
content_tier
stem
options
correct_answer_or_answers_or_order
rationale
is_published
is_draft
created_at
updated_at
source_tag
admin_notes

For case study questions also support:
case_title
case_text
case_tabs
linked_questions

For bowtie questions also support:
condition_options
correct_condition
intervention_options
correct_interventions
monitoring_parameter_options
correct_monitoring_parameter

PART 3: IMPORT VALIDATION RULES

Validate the following before import:

content_tier must equal RN
type must be one of:
multiple_choice
select_all_that_apply
priority
ordered_response
case_study
bowtie

rationale must be present and non-empty
stem must be present
difficulty must be present
category must be present
target_exams must include US RN or Canadian RN or both
question_number must be unique unless admin explicitly allows renumbering
options must match the question type
correct answer data must match the question type

Reject or flag:
missing rationale
unsupported type
empty stem
wrong content_tier
missing target_exams
malformed bowtie structure
malformed case study structure

If rationale is missing, show admin error:
Rationale required before publishing RN question.

PART 4: DUPLICATE DETECTION

Before import, compare incoming questions against existing RN bank using:
normalized stem match
high similarity stem match
same category plus same correct answer plus same rationale similarity
question_number collision

If duplicate likely:
show admin warning
allow skip duplicate
allow import as new variant
allow replace existing question if admin confirms

PART 8: SUPPORTED QUESTION TYPE RENDERING

exactly two interventions selected
one monitoring parameter selected

SYSTEM INSTRUCTION FOR NURSENEST QUESTION IMPORT

CONTENT_TIER: RN
TARGET_EXAMS:
NCLEX-RN (United States)
Canadian RN preparation

QUESTION 621
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Sepsis
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client presents with fever, tachycardia, hypotension, altered mental status, and poor urine output.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Septic shock
Stable dehydration
Heart failure

CORRECT CONDITION
Septic shock

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer broad-spectrum antibiotics
Initiate IV fluid resuscitation
Delay treatment until all cultures result
Restrict fluids

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer broad-spectrum antibiotics
Initiate IV fluid resuscitation

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Serum lactate
Visual acuity
Bowel sounds
Peripheral edema

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Serum lactate

RATIONALE
The client shows classic signs of septic shock with hypoperfusion and organ dysfunction. Early antibiotics and aggressive IV fluids are essential, and lactate helps monitor the severity of tissue hypoxia and response to treatment.

QUESTION 622
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Cardiac
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client reports chest pain, diaphoresis, nausea, and pain radiating to the left arm.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Acute myocardial infarction
Stable angina
Pericarditis

CORRECT CONDITION
Acute myocardial infarction

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer aspirin
Obtain or prepare for ECG and urgent cardiac evaluation
Encourage walking to reduce anxiety
Delay assessment until troponin returns

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer aspirin
Obtain or prepare for ECG and urgent cardiac evaluation

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Cardiac rhythm
Urine color
Bowel elimination
Skin moisture only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Cardiac rhythm

RATIONALE
These symptoms strongly suggest acute myocardial infarction. Aspirin and urgent cardiac evaluation reduce delay in treatment, while cardiac rhythm monitoring is essential because dysrhythmias are a major complication.

QUESTION 623
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Respiratory
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client with COPD becomes increasingly dyspneic, wheezes, uses accessory muscles, and has an oxygen saturation of 84 percent.

CONDITION OPTIONS
COPD exacerbation
Pleural effusion
Panic attack

CORRECT CONDITION
COPD exacerbation

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Provide supplemental oxygen as prescribed
Prepare bronchodilator therapy
Encourage the client to lie flat
Delay treatment until complete imaging is done

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Provide supplemental oxygen as prescribed
Prepare bronchodilator therapy

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Respiratory effort
Bowel sounds
Visual acuity
Capillary refill only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Respiratory effort

RATIONALE
Increasing dyspnea, wheeze, accessory muscle use, and hypoxemia indicate COPD exacerbation. Oxygen and bronchodilator therapy are immediate priorities, and respiratory effort helps identify worsening fatigue and impending respiratory failure.

QUESTION 624
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Neurology
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A client develops sudden facial droop, unilateral weakness, and slurred speech 20 minutes ago.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Acute ischemic stroke
Bell palsy
Migraine aura

CORRECT CONDITION
Acute ischemic stroke

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Activate stroke protocol
Prepare for urgent brain imaging
Encourage oral intake
Delay assessment to see if symptoms resolve

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Activate stroke protocol
Prepare for urgent brain imaging

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Neurologic status
Bowel habits
Skin turgor
Urine glucose

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Neurologic status

RATIONALE
This is a classic acute stroke presentation. Immediate protocol activation and brain imaging are essential to determine reperfusion eligibility, and neurologic monitoring is crucial for detecting deterioration.

QUESTION 625
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Maternal Health
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A pregnant client at 32 weeks has severe headache, blood pressure of 170 over 110, and proteinuria.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Severe preeclampsia
Placenta previa
Gestational diabetes

CORRECT CONDITION
Severe preeclampsia

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Administer prescribed seizure prophylaxis
Monitor blood pressure closely
Encourage unrestricted activity
Delay reassessment because headache is common in pregnancy

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Administer prescribed seizure prophylaxis
Monitor blood pressure closely

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Neurologic status
Hearing changes
Bowel elimination
Visual acuity only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Neurologic status

RATIONALE
Severe hypertension with proteinuria and headache strongly suggests severe preeclampsia. Seizure prophylaxis and close blood pressure monitoring are required, and neurologic assessment helps detect progression toward eclampsia.

QUESTION 626
TYPE: bowtie
CATEGORY: Pediatrics
DIFFICULTY: hard
TARGET_EXAMS: US RN, Canadian RN
CONTENT_TIER: RN

STEM:
A toddler has fever, drooling, muffled voice, and sits leaning forward to breathe.

CONDITION OPTIONS
Epiglottitis
Croup
Bronchiolitis

CORRECT CONDITION
Epiglottitis

INTERVENTION OPTIONS
Maintain airway support and urgent evaluation
Keep the child calm
Perform aggressive throat examination immediately
Force the child to lie flat

CORRECT INTERVENTIONS
Maintain airway support and urgent evaluation
Keep the child calm

MONITORING PARAMETER OPTIONS
Work of breathing
Bowel sounds
Urine ketones
Peripheral pulses only

CORRECT MONITORING PARAMETER
Work of breathing

RATIONALE
Drooling, muffled voice, tripod positioning, and fever are highly concerning for epiglottitis and possible airway obstruction. The child should be kept calm and urgently evaluated while monitoring work of breathing closely.
